requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into contracts with Eugene Barnes, Chicago,
Illinois and Stephen S. Morrill, Chicago, Illinois, whose names I am submitting for consideration as
County Lobbyists. Mr. Barnes and Mr. Morrill will serve for a period of one year beginning December l ,
2005 through November 30, 2006 in the amount of $60,000.00 each, plus expenses not to exceed
$ 10,000.00 each (Accounts 490-260 and 018-260, respectively).
It is important that these individuals be approved as soon as possible in order to guarantee lobbying
services for the next General Assembly.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $140,000.00 ($60,000.00 plus expenses not to exceed $ 10,000.00 - (490-260
Account); and $60,000.00 plus expenses not to exceed $10,000.00 - (0 18-260 Account)]. Contract
Period: December 1, 2005 through November 30, 2006.
Approval of this item would commit Fiscal Year 2006 funds.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the County Purchasing Agent
be authori zed to enter into the requested contracts. The motion carried unanimously.
PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT
Transmitting a Communication, dated December 12, 2005 from
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President, Cook County Board of Commissioners
I am submitting for your approval an ordinance to amend the Taxpayer's Interest Assurance Ordinance
last amended on November 16, 1993. The proposed changes are the collaboration of the Office of the
Chief Financial Officer, the Office of the County Treasurer and the County Auditor. The proposed
changes will align the County with the collateralization requirements of other area governments, as well
as enable the County to generate additional interest income on our deposits.

188

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT

AN ORDINANCE TO AMEND THE
COOK COUNTY TAXPAYERS' INTEREST ASSURANCE ORDINANCE
LAST AMENDED ON NOVEMBER 16, 1993
WHEREAS, the County of Cook is a home rule unit of government as defined in Article VII, Section
6(a) of the 1970 Constitution of the State of Illinois, and as such may exercise any power and perform any
function pertaining to its government and affairs; and
WHEREAS, on March 5, 199 1, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County adopted the "Cook County
Taxpayers' Interest Assurance Ordinance" directing all elected and appointed public officials of Cook
County to invest public funds in their possession or for which they are custodians in interest-beari ng
accounts; and
WHEREAS, the State Treasurer's Act gives the State Treasurer the authority to establish and administer
the Illinois Public Treasurer's Investment Pool (IPTIP) to supplement and enhance the investment
opportunities available to custodians of public funds for public agencies; and
WHEREAS, the State Treasurer is given authority under the State Treasurer's Act to receive public funds
from the custodian of such funds and serve as the custodian's fiscal agent for the purpose of holding and
investing those funds; and
WHEREAS, because of convenience, rate of return and overall security, it is in the best interest of Cook
County to authorize participation in IPTIP; and
WHEREAS, on November 16, 1993. the Board of Commissioners of Cook County desire to amend the
"Cook County Taxpayers' Interest Assurance Ordinance" to authorize Cook County's participation in
IPTIP; and
WHEREAS, the primary objective in managing public funds is the protection of principal; and
WHEREAS, collateralization of public funds by approved depositories through the pledging of securities
is one way to guarantee the safety of public deposits; and
WHEREAS, the posting of collateral in excess of I 02% results in a decrease in interest earned on
deposits; and

WHEREAS, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County desire to amend the "Cook County Taxpayers'
Interest Assurance Ordinance" to at1thorize Cook Cot10ty's partieipation in IPTIP; reduce the
collateralization req uirement from 110% to 102%, to define approved depositories and to establish a
monitoring procedure.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County that the
"Cook County Taxpayers' Interest Assurance Ordinance" shall be amended as follows:
Section 1. This Ordinance shall be known and may be cited as the "Cook County Taxpayers' Interest
Assurance Ordinance."

189

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005

Section 2. All elected and appointed public officials of Cook County are directed to invest public funds in
their possession or for which they are custodians in interest-bearing accounts, except where prohibited by
law or whefe for which compelling economic reasons do not justify the use of an interest-bearing account.
If any public funds are not invested in an interest-bearing account, the elected or appointed public official
shall certify in writing to the Chief Financial Officer and the County Auditor the reason that such funds
have not been invested in an interest-bearing account. The Chief Financial Officer and the County
Auditor will forward to the President of the County Board who, in tum, will forward to the Chairman of
the Audit Committee the correspondence received from the elected or appointed officials indicating why
public funds have not been invested in an interest-bearing account. On an annual basis, the Chief
Financial Officer shall report to the Audit Committee a listing of all depository accounts including the
department number, department name, name of account, depository institution, account number, account
balance, average daily balance, authorized signers, interest rate and any explanation or certification for
any non-interest bearing accounts.
Section 3. The County Auditor shall report to the County Board as part of his an annual audit of the
accounts of each elected and appointed public official (i) the nature and amount of all funds for which
such certifications have been received from elected or appointed public officials, and (ii) the rates of
return received by elected and appointed public officials on invested funds, and (iii) the average daily
balance in the interest-bearing account in order to provide a benchmark against which to evaluate the rate
of return the elected and appointed officials are earning on the funds.
Section 4. Any public funds in the possession or custody of an elected or appointed public official may be
invested in any financial institution approved from time to time by the County Board as a depository of
public funds. The minimum requirements for any financial institution to be an approved depository for
County fund s shall include (i) minimum capital requirement of $ 10 million, (ii) the institution must have
been in operation for at least five years, (iii) located in Cook County, and (iv) meet regulatory
requirement of the Community Reinvestment Act and not engage in predatory lending practices. No
elected or appointed public official shall open any new account in an approved depository without
reporting the opening of such account to the County Auditor and the Chief Financial O fficer of the
County within seven days of the opening of such account.
Section 5. Any elected or appointed public official who invests any public funds in any approved
depository which are in excess of the insured limits of such depository shall require that such depository
provide~ at least 102% collateral ea or provide a surety bond in an amount of 102% on any funds in
excess of the insured ~ limit of such depository, except as provided in Section 6 of this Ordinance.
Section 6. The Cook County Treasurer is authorized to make use of the 111inois Public Treasurer's
Investment Pool (IPTIP), pursuant to 30 ILCS 235/2 (e) ( 1992), on a limited basis facil itate wire transfer
of funds due and owing to Cook County payable by the State of Illinois. Such funds, as they become due
to Cook County, may be invested by the Cook County Treasurer in the IPTIP for a period of time not to
exceed ten calendar days. The collateral requirement on County funds invested by the County Treasurer
in the IPTIP shall not be less than I 02%.
Whenever a public agency deposits any public funds in a financial institution, the public agency shall
enter into an agreement with the financial institution requiring any funds not insured by the Federal
Depository Insurance Corporation to be collateralized by securities, a letter of credit or mortgage backed
securities in an amount equal to at least 102% of the market value of that amount of funds deposited
exceeding the insurance limitation provided by the Federal Depository Insurance Corporation. The letter
of credit must be issued by a financial institution that is rated "A" or better by at least two of the
followi ng rating agencies: Fitch, Moody 's and Standard & Poor' s. Mortgage backed securities used as
collateral must be guaranteed by the Federal Home Loan Bank system, the Federal Home Loan Mortgage
Corporation or the Federal National Mortgage Association.

190

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005

Section 7. Except as provided in Section 6 of this Ordinance, Cook County funds placed in the IPTIP
shall be invested in the same manner, in the same types of investments and subject to the same limitations
provided for the investment of funds in the State Treasury.
Section 8. The Cook County Treasurer, the Chief Financial Officer of Cook County and the County
Comptroller are authorized to execute on behalf of Cook County, an "Application and Agreement to
Participate in the fllinois Public Treasurer's Investment Pool", the terms of which shall not be inconsistent
with this Ordinance.
Section 9. As used in this Ordinance, the tenn "public funds" shall mean current operating funds, special
funds, interest and sinking funds, and funds of any kind or character belonging to or in the custody of any
elected or appointed public official. The County Board may supersede the provisions of the Ordinance
should the authorizing ordinance specify the permitted investments and with respect to similar funds held
in a fiduciary capacity pursuant to statute or specific ordinance.
Section 10. This Ordinance shall be effective upon passage.
Section 11. The amendments to this Ordinance shall be effective upon passage.

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the Proposed Ordinance
Amendment be referred to the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No. 27478 1). The motion carried
unanimously.

COMMISSIONERS
PROPOSED ORDINANCES

Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
MIKE QUIGLEY, FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS, GREGG GOSLIN,
ROBERTO MALDONADO and JOHN P. DALEY, County Commissioners
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
COOK COUNTY FACILITY SMOKING POLICY
WHEREAS, in 1988, the City of Chicago enacted the "Clean Indoor Air Ordinance" that requires all
employers located within Chicago to enact a smoking policy; and
WHEREAS, in response to the City of Chicago Ordinance, the Cook County Board of Commissioners
adopted a resolution setting forth a smoking policy for County facilities; and
WHEREAS, since that time there has been new research as to the effects of secondhand smoke; and
WHEREAS, secondhand smoke contains over 4,000 chemical compounds, of which 200 are known
poisons including carbon monoxide, arsenic, cyanide, benzene and formaldehyde; and
WHEREAS, the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency classifies secondhand smoke as a " Class A
Carcinogen"; and

191

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

WHEREAS, secondhand smoke is the third leading cause of preventable death in America and causes
cancer, stroke, heart disease, SIDS and asthma; and
WHEREAS, employees who work in smoke-filled businesses suffer a 25-50% higher risk of heart attack
and higher rates of death from cardiovascular disease and cancer, as well as increased acute respiratory
disease and measurable decrease in lung function; and
WHEREAS, there is no safe level of exposure to secondhand smoke; and
WHEREAS, (I) the U.S. Surgeon General has determined that the simple separation of smokers and
nonsmokers within the same air space may reduce, but does not eliminate, the exposure of nonsmokers to
secondhand smoke, (2) the Environmental Protection Agency has detennined that second hand smoke
cannot be reduced to safe levels in businesses by high rates of ventilation, (3) air cleaners, which are only
capable of filtering the particulate matter and odors in smoke, do not eliminate the known toxins in
secondhand smoke, (4) ASHRAE (American Society of Heating, Refrigerating and Air Conditioning
Engineers) bases its ventilation standards on totally smoke-free environments because it cannot determine
a safe level of exposure to secondhand smoke, which contains cancer-causing chemicals, and ASHRAE
acknowledges that the technology does not exist that can remove chemicals from the air that cause cancer;
and
WHEREAS, persons with business in County facilities should not be required to subject themselves to
smoke as a part of their conducting business in those facilities; and
WHEREAS, both the City of Chicago "Clean Indoor Air Ordinance" and the " Illinois Clean Indoor Air
Act" permit the banning of smoking in public places; and
WHEREAS, in response to the risks associated with smoking, the Sheriff of Cook County has banned
smoking throughout the Department of Corrections; and
WHEREAS, providing a healthful and safe work place for all employees and member of the public using
County facilities should be given priority over providing a convenient place for persons to smoke.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County that
smoking of cigarettes, cigars, pipes or tobacco in any other fonn is not permitted in any areas of any
facility owned or operated by Cook County, including without limitation those facilities housing
administrative offices, courthouses, detention facilities or jails; and that this ban on smoking applies to all
public areas of Cook County fac ilities as well as all areas used only by County employees or officials,
including without limitation individual offices; and
BE IT FURTHER ORDAINED, that smoking is also prohibited in all vehicles owned or leased by the
County of Cook; and
BE IT FURTHER ORDAINED, that smoking is prohibited within a reasonable distance of 25 feet
outside of an enclosed area, owned or operated by the County of Cook, where smoking is prohibited, so
to prohibit congestion at exits that could constitute a fire hazard in the event of an emergency evacuation
of the building; and
BE IT FURTHER ORDAINED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County directs that all
appropriate County officials, including the Director of Facilities Management, the Chief Administrative
Officer, and other elected officials to implement the foregoing policy.

192

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005
This Resolution supersedes and replaces any and all earlier Resolutions pertaining to the subject of a
smoking policy for Cook County employees and public facilities owned or operated by Cook County.
This Ordinance shall take effect forty-five (45) days from its passage and publication.

Commissioner Quigley, seconded by Commissioner Goslin, moved that the Proposed Ordinance be
referred to the Committee on Health and Hospitals. (Comm. No. 274779). The motion carried
unanimously.

* * * **
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
MIKE QUIGLEY, EARLEAN COLLINS, GREGG GOSLIN, ROBERTO MALDONADO
and JOHN P. DALEY, County Commissioners
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
COOK COUNTY INVOLUNTARY SMOKE REDUCTION ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, secondhand smoke contains over 4,000 chemical compounds, of which 200 are known
poisons including carbon monoxide, arsenic, cyanide, benzene and formaldehyde; and
WHEREAS, the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency classifies secondhand smoke as a "Class A
Carcinogen"; and
WHEREAS, secondhand smoke is the third leading cause of preventable death in America and causes
cancer, stroke, heart disease, SIDS and asthma; and
WHEREAS, employees who work in smoke-filled businesses suffer a 25-50% higher risk of heart attack
and higher rates of death from cardiovascular disease and cancer, as well as increased acute respiratory
disease and measurable decrease in lung function; and
WHEREAS, the Americans with Disabilities Act, which requires that disabled persons have access to
public places and workplaces, deems impaired respiratory function to be a disability and a workplace with
exposure to secondhand smoke could therefore be a violation of the Americans with Disabilities Act; and
WHEREAS, there is no safe level of exposure to secondhand smoke; and
WHEREAS, (I) the U.S. Surgeon General has determined that the simple separation of smokers and
nonsmokers within the same air space may reduce, but does not eliminate, the exposure of nonsmokers to
secondhand smoke, (2) the Environmental Protection Agency has determined that second hand smoke
cannot be reduced to safe levels in businesses by high rates of ventilation, (3) air cleaners, which are only
capable of filtering the particulate matter and odors in smoke, do not eliminate the known toxins in
secondhand smoke, (4) ASHRAE (American Society of Heating, Refrigerating and Air Conditioning
Engineers) bases its ventilation standards on totally smoke-free environments because it cannot detennine
a safe level of exposure to secondhand smoke, which contains cancer-causing chemicals, and ASHRAE
acknowledges that the technology does not exist that can remove chemicals from the air that cause cancer;
and

193

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

WHEREAS, exposure to secondhand smoke costs the nation $5 billion in direct medical costs and $5
billion in indirect medical costs annually; and
WHEREAS, limiting the exposure to secondhand smoke will result in considerable savings to taxpayers
through the reduction of direct and indirect medical costs to County employees and taxpayers utilizing
County health facilities; and
WHEREAS, the states of California, Massachusetts, Rhode Island, Utah, Vennont, Idaho, Connecticut,
South Dakota, Maine, Delaware and Florida adopted protective clean indoor air laws that eliminate
workers', patrons' and visitors' exposure to secondhand smoke; and
WHEREAS, since 2002, 90 independent studies have concluded that there is either no impact or there is
a positive impact after the implementation of smoke-free restaurant/bar Jaws and Jaws banning smoking in
the workplace; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners finds and declares that the purposes of this
Ordinance are (1) to protect the public health and welfare by prohibiting smoking in all public places and
places of employment, and (2) the guarantee the right of nonsmokers to breathe smoke-free air which
shall have priority over the desire to smoke.
NOW, THEREFORE,
COMMISSIONERS:
Section 1:

BE

IT

ORDAINED

BY

THE

COOK

COUNTY

BOARD

OF

Title

This Chapter shall be known as the Cook County Involuntary Smoke Reduction Ordinance.
Section 2:

Interpretation with Other Laws

Nothing in this Chapter overrides any existing elimination of smoking that is already covered by fire code
restrictions.
Section 3:

Definitions

T he following words and phrases, wherein used m Sections l through 18, shall have the following
meanmgs:
" Arcade" means a place of amusement, which contains four or more automatic am usement devices
and is not licensed to serve alcoholic liquor.
"Attached Bar/Tavern" means an establishment that is devoted to the serving of alcoholic beverages
for consumption by guests and patrons on the premises and does not have an on-site kitchen to
prepare food. Food service is limited to providing snack items or commercially prepared or
wrapped foods that require no preparation.
" Business" means any sole proprietorship, partnership, joint venture, corporation, limited liability
company or other business entity fanned for profit-making purposes, including without limitation
retai l establishments where goods or services are sold as well as professional corporations and other
entities where legal, medical, dental, engineering, architectural, or other professional services are
delivered.

194

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005

" Employee" means any person who is employed by an employer in consideration for direct or
indirect monetary wages or profit and a person who volunteers his or her services for a non-profit
entity.
" Employer" means any person, business, partnership, association, corporation, including without
limitation a municipal corporation, trust, or non-profit entity that employs the services of one or
more individual persons.
"Enclosed Area" means all space between a floor and ceiling that is enclosed on all sides by solid
walls or windows (exclusive of doorways), which extend from the floor to the ceiling including
without limitations lobbies and corridors.
" Heath-Care Facility" means any office or institution providing care or treatment of diseases,
whether physical, mental, or emotional, or other medical, physiological, or psychological
conditions, including without limitation hospitals, rehabilitation hospitals, clinics, nursing homes,
homes for the aging or chronically ill, laboratories, and offices of surgeons, chiropractors, physical
therapists, physicians, dentist and all specialists within these professions. The definition shall
include all waiting rooms, hallways, private rooms, semiprivate rooms, and wards within health
care facilities.
" Place of Employment" means any enclosed area under the control of a public or private employer
that employees frequent during the course of employment, including without limitation work areas,
employee lounges, restrooms, conference rooms, classrooms, employee cafeterias, hallways and
vehicles. A private residence is not a " Place of Employment" unless it is used as a childcare, adult
day care, health care facility, or home-based business of any kind open to the public.
" Public Place" means any enclosed area to which the public is invited or in which the public is
permitted, including without limitation banks, education facilities, government buildings, health
care facilities, laundromats, museums, public transportation facilities, reception areas, restaurants,
bars/taverns, retail food production and marketing establishments, retail service establishments,
retail stores, shopping malls, sports arenas, theaters, and waiting rooms. A private residence is not a
" Public Place" unless it is used as a childcare, ad ult daycare, health care facility or home-based
business of any kind open to the public.
" Private Function" means a gathering of persons for the purpose of deliberation, education,
instruction, entertainment, amusement or dining where membership or specific invitation is a
prerequisite to entry and where the event is not intended to be open to the public.
" Restaurant" means an eating establishment, including without limitation coffee shops, cafeterias,
sandwich shops, and private and public school cafeterias that gives, or offers for sale, food to the
public, guests or employees, as well as kitchens and catering facilities in which food is prepared on
the premises for serving elsewhere. The term " Restaurant" shall include, if applicable, an attached
bar/tavern.
" Retail Tobacco Store" means any retail store utilized primarily for the sale of tobacco products and
accessories and in which the sale of other products is merely incidental and where no one under I 8
is permitted.
"Service Line" means any indoor line at which one (I) or more persons are waiting for or receiving
services of any kinds, whether or not the service involves the exchange of money.

195

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

"Shopping Mall" means any enclosed walkway or hall area that serves to connect retail or
professional establishments.
"Smoking" means inhaling, exhaling, burning, or carrying any lighted cigar, cigarette, pipe, weed,
hookah, or other lighted tobacco product in any manner or in any form.
"Sports Arena" or "Recreational Area" means any sports pavilion, stadium, gymnasium, health spa,
boxing arena, swimming pool, roller and ice rink, bowling alley and other similar places where
members of the general public assemble either to engage in physical exercise, participate in athletic
or recreational competition or activity, or to witness sports, cultural, recreational or other events.

Section 4:

County-Owned Facilities

All enclosed vehicles and facilities, including without limitation buildings and vehicles owned, leased, or
operated by the County of Cook shall be subject to the provision of this Chapter.

Section 5:

Prohibition of Smoking in Public Places

Smoking shall be prohibited in all enclosed public places and places of employment within the County of
Cook, including without limitation the following places:
I.

Arcades.

2.

Aquariums, galleries, libraries, and museums.

3.

Bars/taverns.

4.

Bingo facilities.

5.

Convention facilities.

6.

Facilities primarily used for exhibiting a motion picture, stage, drama, lecture, musical recital,
or other similar performance.

7.

Health care facilities, adult day care facilities, and nursing homes.

8.

Day care centers, nursery schools, elementary schools, high schools, community colleges,
technical training establishments, specialty schools, colleges, and universities.

9.

Lobbies, hallways and other common areas in apartment buildings, condominiums and enclosed
common areas in trailer parks.

10.

Polling places.

11.

Public transportation facilities under the authority of government agencies, including without
limitation buses, trains, taxi cabs, and limousines, and ticket boarding and waiting areas of
public transit stations.

I 2.

Restaurants, including if applicable, an attached bar/tavern.

13.

Restrooms, lobbies, reception areas, hallways, and other enclosed common-use areas.

196

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

14.

Public elevators and all retail stores where merchandise is displayed and offered for sale.

I 5.

Rooms, chambers, places of meeting or public assembly, including without limitation school
buildings, under the control of an agency, board, commissioner, committee or council or a
political subdivision of the State, to the extent the place is subject to the jurisdiction of the
County.

16.

Service lines.

I 7.

Shopping malls.

18.

Sports arenas or recreational areas, including without limitation enclosed places in outdoor
areas.

19.

Grocery stores.

20.

Public meetings.

21.

Gymnasiums.

22.

Government vehicles used for County business such as maintenance trucks or fleet vehicles.

23.

Gaming facilities.

24.

Public and private school buildings.

Section 6:

Prohibition of Smoking in Places of Employment

This prohibition on smoking shall be communicated to all existing employees by the effect date of this
Chapter and to all prospective employees upon their application for employment.

Section 7:

Reasonable Distance

Smoking is prohibited within a reasonable distance of 25 feet outside of an enclosed area where smoking
is prohibited, so as to prohibit congestion at exits that could constitute a fire hazard in the event of an
emergency evacuation of the building. This Section does not prohibit someone who is in the course of
passing by or drivi ng by in a car.

Section 8:

Where Smoking is not Regulated.

Notwithstanding any other provision of this Article to the contrary, the following areas shall be exempt
from the provisions of Sections I through 18.
I. Private residences, except when used as a licensed childcare, adult care facility, health care
facility, or a home-based business of any kind open to the public.
2. Hotel and motel sleeping rooms that are rented to guests and are designated as smoking rooms
provided, however, that not more than twenty-five percent (25%) of the rooms rented to guests in
a hotel or motel may be so designated.

197

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005

3. Retail tobacco stores, provided that smoke from these places does not infiltrate into areas where
smoking is prohibited under any provisions of Sections 1 through 18.

Section 9:

Declaration of Establishment as Non-smoking

Notwithstanding any other provision of this Chapter, an owner, operator, manager, or other person in
control of an establishment, facility, or outdoor area may declare that entire establishment, facility, or
outdoor area as a non-smoking place.
Smoking shall be prohibited in any place in which a sign confonning to the requirements of this Chapter
is posted.

Section 10:

Posting of Signs

A. Every public place and place of employment where smoking is prohibited by this Chapter shall
have posted at entrance a conspicuous sign clearly stating that smoking is prohibited.

B. The operator, manager or other person having control of an area where smoking is prohibited by
this Chapter shall remove all ashtrays and other smoking paraphernalia intended for use where
smoking is prohibited.
When applying for an original or renewed food dispensing establishment license, the owner or operator of
a restaurant shall also submit a notarized statement declaring that "No Smoking" signs have been posted
with the following language: " Pursuant to the Municipal Code of the County of Cook, a ny person
smoking shall be subject to a fine of not less than $100 and not more than $500."

Section 11:

Non-retaliation

No person or employer shall discharge, refuse to hire, or in any manner retaliate against an employee,
applicant for employment, or customer because that employee, applicant, or customer exercises any
rights afforded by this Chapter or reports or attempts to prosecute a violation of this Chapter.

Section 12:

Enforcement

A. This Chapter shall be enforced by the Cook County Department of Public Health or an authorized

designee.
B. Notice of the provisions Section 1 through 18 shall be given to all applicants for a business
license in Unincorporated Cook County.
C. Any citizen who desires to register a complaint under Sections 1 through 18 may initiate
enforcement with the Cook County Department of Public Heath.
D. The Cook County Department of Public Health or their designees shall , while an establishments is
undergoing otherwise mandated inspections, inspect for compliance with Sections 1 through 18.
E. Any owner, manager, operator, or employee of an establishment regulated by this Chapter shall
inform persons violating Sections I through 18 of the appropriate provisions thereof.

198

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005
F. In addition to the remedies provided by the provisions of Sections I through 18, the Cook County
Department of Public Health or any person aggrieved by the failure of the owner, operator,
manager of other person in control of a public place or a place of employment to comply with the
provisions of this Section may apply for injunctive relief to enforce those provision in any court
of competent jurisdiction.
Section 13:

Violations and Penalties

A. A person who smokes in an area where smoking is prohibited by Sections 1 through 18 shall be

guilty of an infraction, punishable by a fine not less than one hundred dollars ($100) and not more
than five hundred dollars ($500).
B. A person who owns, manages, operates or otherwise controls a public place or place of
employment and who fails to comply with the provisions of Sections 1 through 18 shall be guilty
of an infraction, punishable by:
1.

A fine not exceeding one hundred dollars $100) for the first violation.

2.

A fine not more than five hundred dollars ($500) for the second violation within one (I)
year of the first violation.

3.

A fine not more than two thousand five hundred dollars ($2500) for each additional
violation within one (1) year and a sixty (60) day suspension or revocation of any permit or
license issued to the person for the premises on which the violation occurred.

C. Each day on which a violation of Section 1 through 18 occurs shall be considered a separate and
distinct violation.
D. Revenues collected pursuant to Sections I through 18 will be dedicated to enforcement and public
education, including the 890-298 account for funding of lung related illness programs.
Section 14:

Public Education

The Cook County Department of Public Health shall engage in a continuing program to explain and
clarify the purposes and requirements of Sections 1 through 18 to citizens affected by it, and to guide
owners, operators, and managers in their compliance with it.
Section 15:

Government Agency Cooperation

The President and the Board of Commissioners of Cook County shall annually request that other
governmental and additional agencies having facilities located within the County of Cook establish local
operating procedures in cooperation and compliance with this Chapter. This includes urging all federal,
state, city, special district and school district agencies to update their existing smoking regulations to be
consistent with the current health findings regarding secondhand smoke.
Section 16:

Other Applicable Laws

This Chapter shall not be interpreted or be construed to permit smoking where it is otherwise restricted by
other applicable laws.

199

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005

Section 17:

Severability

If any provision, clause, sentence or paragraph of this Chapter or the application thereof to any person or
circumstances shall be held invalid by a court of competent jurisdiction, such invalidity shall not affect
the other provisions of this Chapter which can be given effect without the invalid provision or application,
and to this end the provisions of this Chapter are declared to be severable.

Section 18:

Effective Date

This Ordinance shall take effect sixty days (60) days from its passage and publication.

Commissioner Quigley, seconded by Commissioner Goslin, moved that the Proposed Ordinance be
referred to the Committee on Health and Hospitals. (Comm. No. 274780). The motion carried
unanimously.

PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT

AMENDMENT TO SECTION 2.12 OF THE
"AMENDED COOK COUNTY ETHICS ORDINANCE"
WHEREAS, the County of Cook, Illinois is a home rule unit oflocal government pursuant to Article VII,
Section 6(a) of the 1970 Illinois Constitution, and pursuant to the authority therein granted, may exercise
any power and perform any function pertaining to its government and affairs; and
WHEREAS, on August 3, 1993, pursuant to its home rule powers, the Board of Commissioners of Cook
County adopted an Ordinance establishing a Code of Ethical Conduct for Cook County officials and
employees which Ordinance was effective September 1, 1993; and
WHEREAS, effecti ve November 19, 2003, the General Assembly of Illinois enacted the State Officials
and Employees Ethics Act, 5 ILCS 430 et seq., ("State Ethics Act") which establishes a code of ethical
conduct for all state officers, members of the Illinois General Assembly, and state employees; and
WHEREAS, the State Ethics Act also provides that within six months of its enactment, Cook County
shall regulate the political activities of certain officials and employees of Cook County, and the
solicitation and acceptance of gifts by the offering and making of gifts to officials and employees of Cook
County in a manner no less restrictive than the provisions of the State Ethics Act; and
WHEREAS, it is essential to the proper operation of representative government that public officials and
employees be independent and impartial; that public office and employment not be used for personal gain,
and that the public have full confidence in the integrity and fair and honest administration of government;
and
WHEREAS, public officials and employees serve their government in a fiduciary capacity, and must act
at all times to avoid conflicts of interest, impropriety, or even the appearance of impropriety; and

200

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 2 1, 2005

WHEREAS, a Code of Ethical Conduct will assist officials and employees of Cook County to conform
their conduct to the highest acceptable standards and to properly discharge their fiduciary duties; and
WHEREAS, compliance with a Code of Ethical Conduct will improve standards of public service and
strengthen the confidence of the people of Cook County in their government.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS OF COOK
COUNTY, ILLINOIS, THAT THE CODE OF ETHICAL CONDUCT FOR COOK COUNTY IS
AMENDED AS FOLLOWS:

ARTICLE II

2.12

Political Activity
(a)

No official or employee shall compel, coerce or intimidate any County official or
employee to make or refrain from making any political contribution. No official shall
directly solicit any political contribution from his or her employees or the spouses of or
immediate family living with his or her employees. Nothing in this subsection (a) shall
be construed to prevent any official or employee from voluntarily making a contribution
or from receiving a voluntary contribution.

(b)

No employee with contract management authority shall serve on the political fundraising
committee of any elected official or candidate for County office.

(c)

County employees shall not intentionally perform any prohibited political activity during
any compensated time (other than vacation, personal, or compensatory time oft). County
employees shall not intentionally misappropriate any County property or resources by
engaging in any prohibited political activity for the benefit of any campaign for elective
office or any political organization.
(I)

In the event a County employee intentionally misappropriates any County property
or resources and such resources are found to have been used in the furtherance of
political activity on behalf of that elected official, the elected official on whose
behalf such resources were expended shall be required to reimburse the County an
amount equal to the misappropriated resources used in such political activity.

(d)

At no time shall any official or employee intentionally misappropriate the services of any
County employee by requiring that employee to perfonn any prohibited political activity
(i) as part of that employee's County duties, (ii) as a condition of County employment,
or (iii) during any time off that is compensated by the County (such as vacation,
personal, or compensatory time oft).

(e)

A County employee shall not be required at any time to participate in any prohibited
political activity in consideration for that employee being awarded any additional
compensation or employee benefit, in the fonn of a salary adjustment, bonus,
compensatory time off, continued employment, or otherwise.

(t)

A County employee shall not be awarded any additional compensation or employee
benefit, in the fonn of a salary adjustment, bonus, compensatory time off, continued
employment, or otherwise, in consideration for the employee's participation in any
prohibited political activity.

201

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

(g)

Nothing in this Section prohibits activities that are otherwise appropriate for a County
employee to engage in as a part of his or her official County employment duties or
activities that are undertaken by an employee on a voluntary basis as permitted by law.

This Ordinance Amendment shall be effective upon passage.

PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, pursuant to 55 ILCS 5/ l-6003, shall have the
duty "to take and order suitable proper measures for the prosecuting and defending of all suits to be
brought by or against" Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the State's Attorney of Cook County, pursuant to 55 lLCS 5/3-9005(a)(4), shall have the
duty " to defend all actions and proceedings brought against his county, or against any county or State
office, in his official capacity, within his county; and
WHEREAS, in the course of such representation in Workers' Compensation matters, the State's
Attorney is frequently advised of settlement offers which provide the opportunity to terminate such
litigation to the mutual satisfaction of the parties; and
WHEREAS, the amounts involved in such offers may be of such small magnitude that it would not be in
the County's best interests to carry the matter to trial ; and
WHEREAS, currently, the State's Attorney of Cook County does not exercise any authority in any
amount to settle Workers' Compensation actions without the approval of the Board of Commissioners;
and
WHEREAS, establishing the State's Attorney 's authority to resolve Workers' Compensation claims at
$25,000.00 allows the State's Attorney to resolve certain Workers' Compensation litigation in the
County's best interest; and
WHEREAS, the Illinois Industrial Commission has changed its name to the Illinois Workers'
Compensation Commission effective January 1, 2005, and the Subcommittee of the Finance Committee
which considers Workers' Compensation claims has been heretofore designated the " Industrial Claims
Subcommittee''.

202

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County hereby
delegates to the State's Attorney of Cook County the authority to settle Workers' Compensation actions
in which the County may be concerned or against any County or State office, in his official capacity,
within this County, provided that such settlement does not commit the County to an expenditure in excess
of $25 ,000.00. Upon request, the State's Attorney shall provide information regarding the basis of such
settlements to any Commissioner.

referred to the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No. 274782). The motion carried unanimously.

PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, pursuant to 55 ILCS 5/ 1-6003, shall have the
duty "to take and order suitable proper measures for the prosecuting and defending of all suits to be
brought by or against" Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the State's Attorney of Cook County, pursuant to 55 ILCS 5/3-9005(a)(4), shall have the
duty "to defend all actions and proceedings brought against his county, or against any county or State
officer, in his official capacity, within his county; and
WHEREAS, in the course of such representation, the State's Attorney is frequently advised of settlement
offers which provide the opportunity to terminate such litigation to the mutual satisfaction of the parties;
and
WHEREAS, on June 21, 1982, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County adopted Resolution 82-R242 authorizing the State's Attorney of Cook County to settle all actions in which the County may be
concerned, provided that "such settlement neither commits the County to an expenditure in excess of
$5,000.00 nor waives an amount in excess of $5,000.00 due to the County in an action brought on its
behalf'; and
WHEREAS, on May 2, 1995, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County adopted Resolution 95-R188 increasing the authority provided to the State's Attorney of Cook County to $10,000.00 to resolve all
actions in which the County may be concerned; and
WHEREAS, increasing the State's Attorney's authority to $25,000.00 enhances the State's Attorney's
ability to resolve litigation in the County's best interest.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County hereby
increase the authority previously conferred upon the State's Attorney of Cook County by Resolution 95R-188, to an amount which does not exceed $25,000.00. Upon request, the State's Attorney shall provide
information regarding the basis of such settlements to any Commissioner.

203

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005

Co-Sponsored by
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER, FORREST CLAYPOOL,
EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY, ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN,

BOBBIE L. STEELE and LARRY SUFFREDIN, County Commissioners
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
COOK COUNTY RUBBERIZED ASPHALT PILOT PROJECT
WHEREAS, rubberized asphalt, also known as asphalt-rubber or A-R, is a blend of asphalt cement,
reclaimed tire rubber, and certain additives, in which the rubber component is at least 15 percent by
weight of the total blend; and
WHEREAS, rubberized asphalt is routinely used in paving projects in Arizona, California, and Texas,
among other states; and
WHEREAS, use of rubberized asphalt takes scrap tires out of the waste stream, alleviating the
environmental and fiscal costs of tire disposal; and
WHEREAS, every lane mile of roadway constructed with rubberized asphalt requires between 500 and
2,000 used tires; and
WHEREAS, repaving just five percent of the nation' s roads each year with rubberi zed asphalt would
remove all scrap tires from the waste stream; and
WHEREAS, rubberized asphalt reduces highway noise by 60 percent compared to conventional asphalt,
according to a study conducted by Sacramento County, California; and
WHEREAS, rubberized asphalt is used successfully in cold climates, including the Sierra Nevada
mountains in California and areas in Arizona at elevations exceeding 7 ,000 feet, where winter
temperatures dip to -20 degrees Fahrenheit; and
WHEREAS, increased use of rubberized asphalt by local governments such as Cook County could have
a transformative effect on the market for paving materials, given local governments' status among the
largest purchasers of goods and services in the United States; and

204

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

WHEREAS, rubberized asphalt is more durable and therefore more economical than conventional
asphalt, with several recent studies confirming that rubberized asphalt has lower life-cycle costs; and
WHEREAS, roads built with rubberized asphalt will last longer than conventionally-constructed roads,
reducing the frequency with which traffic is disrupted by road reconstruction projects; and
WHEREAS, a study by the Arizona Department of Transportation found that 10-year maintenance costs
for rubberized asphalt were $500 per lane-mile, compared to $1,400 per Jane-mile for conventional
asphalt; and
WHEREAS, widespread use of rubberized asphalt by Cook County has the potential to save taxpayers
money by reducing spending on road construction and repair over the Jong term.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of
Commissioners, that the Highway Department is hereby directed to select a capital improvement project
related to roads, parking lots, sidewalks, biking or walking paths, or other pedestrian or vehicular
facilities, for a pilot project in which rubberized asphalt shall be used in place of conventional asphalt.
Such project shall feature at least 2,000 square feet of rubberi zed asphalt and a similarly sized patch of
conventional asphalt, to enable comparisons. Such project shall be selected by the Highway Department
within 6 months of the passage of this Resolution and completed within 12 months of the passage of this
Resolution; and
BE IT FURTHER ORDAINED RESOLVED, that the Highway Department report back to the Board
no later than 3 months after completion of the project with an initial evaluation of the perfonnance of
rubberized asphalt and quarterly reports thereafter; and
BE IT FURTHER ORDAINED RESOLVED, that this OnliRaRee Resolution is hereby repealed 3
years after it is enacted into law.

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Quigley, moved that the Proposed Resolution, as
amended be referred to the Committee on Roads and Bridges (Comm . No. 274784) and the Committee on
Environmental Control (Comm. No. 274785). The motion carried unanimously.

Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
GREGG GOSLIN, County Commissioner
Co-Sponsored by
JERRY BUTLER, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIM S,
BOBBIE L. STEELE and LARRY SUFFREDIN, County Commissioners
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

NEW REAL ESTATE TAX BILL PUBLIC SAFETY LINE ITEM
WHEREAS, Illinois Compiled Statutes Chapter 35 220/20-15 clearly defines the purpose of the property
tax bill as providing taxpayers with detailed information about where and how their tax dollars are spent;
and

205

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005

WHEREAS, the number of line items on the Cook County property tax bill are not reflective of the
actual services rendered by Cook County government; and
WHEREAS, the tax bill currently has a separate "Cook County Health Facilities" line-item on tax bills
which could be utilized to reflect the true cost of providing health services with a corresponding deletion
of said Health Facilities costs from the " County of Cook" tax line item; and
WHEREAS, in an effort to make transparent the cost of services for Public Safety a new line item should
be added to property tax bills specifically to fund public safety services with a corresponding deletion of
said Public Safety costs from the " County of Cook" tax line item; and
WHEREAS, the Public Safety line item would be comprised of the same agencies and departments as the
Public Safety Fund in the County ' s tax levy which accounts for approximately 38.6% of FY 2005
revenue; and
WHEREAS, the Public Safety line item should include the County' s criminal justice system : jails, courts
and related services generally found under the auspices of the Cook County Sheriffs Office, Clerk of the
Circuit Court, the Bureau of Public Safety and Judicial Coordination and the Office of the Chief Judge;
and
WHEREAS, this new line item would clearly show taxpayers the costs of providing services such as the
court system and corrections which the County is required to provide; and
WHEREAS, the corresponding figure or cost of Public Safety would be dedicated to providing these
services and therefore cannot be diverted elsewhere; and
WHEREAS, adding this new line item to Cook County Property Tax Bills is consistent with the Illinois
State Statutes' purpose of providing taxpayers with a clear understanding of where tax dollars are spent.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board encourages the County Clerk
to create a new line item for Public Safety on the Cook County tax bill initiating on the 2nd installment of
the FY 2005 tax bill for the benefit of all property taxpayers.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Goslin, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
refen-ed to the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No. 274786). The motion carried unanimously.

* * * * *
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
CARL R. HANSEN, County Commissioner
Co-Sponsored by
LARRY SUFFREDIN , County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, on January 22, 2004, the Cook County Board of Commissioners approved an amendment to
the Cook County Animal Control Ordinance regarding vicious and dangerous dogs; and

206

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

WHEREAS, this amendment followed and was modeled after House Bill 184, "An Act Regarding
Vicious Dogs," sponsored by State Representative Angelo "Skip" Saviano, which was approved by the
lllinois State Legislature and signed into law by the Governor of the State of Illinois on Tuesday, August
19, 2003;and
WHEREAS, this legislation provided additional responsibilities upon neglectful or malicious dog owners
and additional penalties on such dog owners for the vicious conduct towards humans and other animals;
and
WHEREAS, the amendment to the Cook County Animal Control Ordinance included the following
definition ofa "vicious dog": (Section 20- 10, A.13.) " ... means a dog that, without justification, attacks a
person and causes serious physical injury or death or any individual dog that has been found to be a
' dangerous dog' upon three separate occasions"; and
WHEREAS, this amendment also included the following definition of a "dangerous dog": (Section 2010, A.3.) " .... means any individual dog when unmuzzled, unleashed, or unattended by its owner or
custodian that behaves in a manner that a reasonable person would believe poses a serious and unjustified
imminent threat of serious physical injury or death to a person or companion animal in a public place";
and
WHEREAS, according to the Cook County Department of Animal Control, of the 4,000 dog bites
documented by their office for the calendar year 2005 through September I, 2005, 560 those were from
Pitbulls/Pitbull mixes, 440 of those were from Gennan Shepherd/German Shepherd mixes, and 56 of
those were from Rottweillers; and
WHEREAS, within that same period, two human deaths were caused by Pitbulls, one human death was
caused by a German Shepherd, and one human death was caused by a Rottweiller in Cook County; and
WHEREAS, many local governments, including the City of Chicago, are considering the imposition of a
ban on particular breeds of dogs that are more prone to violent human attacks; and
WHEREAS, on December 6, 2005 , the Village Board of Mount Prospect unanimously approved
Resolution No. 55-05, A Resolution Calling for County Action with Respect to Vicious Animals, in
which they call upon the County Board of Cook County to create and adopt an ordinance that
appropriately defines and prohibits or strictly regulates the breeding or keeping of vicious animals
throughout the County for the protection of all residents; now, therefore,
BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does hereby request that the
Cook County Department of Animal Control, in coordination with the Office of the State's Attorney,
review the resolution brought forth by the Village of Mount Prospect on this subject and identify any
potential revisions to the Cook County Animal Control Ordinance that could enhance the safety measures
currently employed in the Ordinance.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Suffredin, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Public Health Subcommittee. (Comm. No. 274787). The motion carried unanimously.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

* * * * *
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
FORREST CLAYPOOL, MIKE QUIGLEY and LARRY SUFFREDfN, County Commissioners
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
A RESOLUTION CALLING ON COOK COUNTY TO
CONDUCT HEARINGS INTO COUNTY HIRING PROCESS
WHEREAS, the County of Cook, Illinois is a home rule unit of local government pursuant to Article VII,
Section 6(a) of the 1970 Illinois Constitution, and pursuant to the authority therein granted, may exercise
any power and peform any function pertaining to its government and affairs; and
WHEREAS, the recent arrest on a criminal complaint of a President' s Office of Employment Training
(POET) employee alleged that the charged employee was hired at the insistence of an aide to President
John Stroger, over the objections of departmental bosses; and
WHEREAS, a State's Attorney probe revealed the POET employee had an extensive criminal record of
I 0 felony convictions for forgery, theft, and robbery and, after 7 years as a POET employee has been
charged with stealing $180,000 from the County; and
WHEREAS, county taxpayers have the right to know how the county hiring process works, who has
legal authority to hire employees, and what procedures are followed to ensure compliance with the law.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners calls on
President John H. Stroger, Jr. to hold a hearing for the purpose of questioning administration officials in
charge of personnel and other individuals referenced in the state's attorney's criminal complaint with the
goal of detennining how the hiring process in county government is conducted.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Claypool, seconded by Commissioner Suffredin, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Committee on Legislation and Intergovernmental Relations. (Comm. No. 274789). The
motion carried unanimously.

AGREEMENT
Transmitting a Communication, dated December 13, 2005
DANIEL J. COUGHLIN, Executive Director, Judicial Advisory Council
requesting authorization to enter into Cook County Mobile Video and Data Communications Network
Participation Agreements with the following municipalities as part of the Board approved Federal Fiscal
Year 2004 Urban Area Security Initiative Grant with the Illinois Emergency Management Agency funded
by the U.S. Department of Homeland Security. The Cook County Board approved this grant on May 4,
2004 and just recently approved the extension of this grant on December 6, 2005 .
The twenty municipalities identified for this Phase II roll-out were the first to fonnally respond, in the
affirmative to an announcement by the Judicial Advisory Council seeking municipalities ready to
participate in Phase I I of the County' s Interoperable Communication System and, together with the
municipalities currently participating in the System, they contribute to a broad geographic distribution of
participants in the various sectors of Cook County. If funds pennit, the County may be able to include
additional municipalities in Phase II. These participation agreements provide for the municipalities to
participate in the installation and maintenance of the County's interoperable communication system as
described in detail in the County' s contracts providing for the purchase and installation of the system.

228

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

and that the Executive Director of the Cook County Judicial Advisory Council, or his designee, on behalf
of Cook County, be authorized to execute any all necessary documents to further the initiative therein,
including, but not limited to, the participation agreements with the identified municipalities and with
additional municipalities, if funds permit, and any modification thereto.

DEPARTMENT OF PUBLIC HEAL TH
GRANT AWARD ADDENDUM
Transmitting a Communication, dated November 22, 2005 from
STEPHEN A. MARTTN, JR., Ph.D., M.P.H., Chief Operating Officer, Department of Public Health
requesting authorization to accept a supplemental award in the amount of $67 ,313.00 and an extension
from January I, 2006 through February 28, 2006 to a grant from the Illinois Department of Public Health
(IDPH). This program will test Culex mosquitoes and dead crows and blue jays for West Nile virus, and
includes the control of larval mosquitoes of the genus Culex, the primary carrier of the West Nile virus
and St. Louis encephalitis for the Cook County Department of Public Health.
The authorization to accept the original grant was given on March 15, 2005 by the Cook County Board of
Commissioners in the amount of $540,275.00. The grant extension from July 1, 2005 through December
31, 2005 was approved May 17, 2005.
The Budget Department has reviewed this item, and all requisite documents have been submitted.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Supplemental Grant Award: $67,3 13.00. Funding period extension:
January I, 2006 through February 28, 2006.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the request of the Chief
Operating Officer of the Department of Public Health be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

Transmitting a Communication, dated November 29, 2005 from
JOHNNY C. BROWN, Chief Operating Officer, Stroger Hospital of Cook County
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with the Cardiovascular
Surgeons, Ltd., Chicago, Illinois, for the Department of Surgery, Division of Pediatric Surgery for
attending physician coverage consultation services. This surgical group will provide pediatric surgery
coverage as required for a Level I designated Pediatric Trauma Center and participate in the inpatient and
outpatient services on an as needed basis. The group will provide 24 hour on-call coverage and clinic
support. Primary emphasis will be on inpatient emergency and trauma surgery coverage for the NICU,
PICU and pediatric eardiae ward~ in cases of pediatric cardiac anomalies.
Reason:

This group have completed training in cardiothoracic surgery and have had extensive subspecialty training in pediatric cardiac surgery. This group also provides coverage in the west
side medical center for Rush University Medical Center and the University of Illinois Medical
Center.
To maintain the Level I status as a pediatric trauma center, Illinois Department of Public
Health guidelines dictate that we must have availability of a pediatric cardiac surgeon on call
24 hours per day for traumatic cardiac emergencies.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $150,000.00 (Year 1 - $75,000.00; and Year 2 - $75,000.00). Contract period:
January 1, 2006 through December 31 , 2007. (897-272 Account). Requisition No. 68970413.
Approval of this item would commit Fiscal Year 2006 and future year funds.
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that request of the Chief Operating
Officer of Stroger Hospital of Cook County be approved, as amended and that the County Purchasing
Agent be authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Gorman, moved to accept the Substitute
Ordinance for Communication No. 272884. The motion carried.
Chairman Daley asked the Secretary to the Board to read the notice of the public hearing into the record.
Chairman Daley then asked the Secretary to the Board to call upon the registered public speaker.
I.

Matthew F. Walsh - Deputy Chief, Cook County Sheriffs Police

Vice Chainnan Steele inquired how the Ordinance defines the scope of enforceable area.

262

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

Commissioner Suffredin replied that enforceable area is defined under Section 13-74, Right to Inspect
and under Section 13-75, Penalty for Ordinance Violation. The State's Attorney's Office has determined
that private property is not an enforceable area. Enforceable areas are comprised of public streets,
parking Jots that are open to pedestrians and anywhere that Cook County Sheriffs police are invited onto
the property.
Vice Chairman Steele inquired what measures are taken to ensure that fines are paid by violators.
Commissioner Suffredin responded fines are enforced in the Circuit Court. Additionally, the fined person
will have to provide proof that he/she has purchased a vehicle sticker.
Vice Chairman Steele inquired as to the cost of the fines.
Commissioner Suffredin replied the judge determines all fines within the following parameters: the fine
for the Jack of a vehicle sticker is, at minimum, $75 per offense. If a person steals a vehicle sticker, the
fine ranges from $200 to $500.

Vice Chairman Steele, seconded by Commissioner Gorman, moved to amend Section 13-75(c) of the
Substitute Ordinance by inserting "nor more than $150 per offense" at the end of the first sentence.
The motion to amend carried, and Section 13-75(c) now reads as follows:
(c) Penalty for Failure to Properly Display Sticker
Any owner, driver or motor vehicle in violation of these provisions
requiring a license shall be fined not less than seventy-five dollars
($75.00) per offense nor more than one hundred fifty dollars ($ J 50) per
offense.
In response to Commissioner Hansen's concern relative to Section 13-74, Assistant State's Attorney
Helen Haynes, suggested additional language in Section 13-74, Right to Inspect, as referenced in the
following motion.

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Suffredin, moved to amend Section 13-74 by
inserting "registered to an address in unincorporated Cook County" after "any vehicle" and
inserting "Cook County" after "not displaying a". The motion to amend carried, and Section 13-74
now reads as follows :
13-74 Right to Inspect
The Cook County Sheriffs Police are hereby authorized to issue
citations to any vehicle registered to an address in unincorporated Cook
County on the public way in unincorporated Cook County that is not
displaying a Cook County vehicle sticker and furthermore, officers of
the Cook County Sheriffs Police shall have the authority to enter the
following places for purposes of ascertaining whether vehicles parked
therein are in compliance with this Ordinance and issue citations
accordingly:

263

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

ill

Any parking lot that is open to pedestrian traffic.

Nothing in this section authorizes any officer to force, break, or remove
any lock or door in order to gain entry to any of the foregoing places.
In response to an inquiry by Commissioner Sims, Commissioner Suffredin clarified that Forest Preserve
police have no authority under this Ordinance because they do not have patrol authority outside of Forest
Preserve District lands. However, because some Forest Preserve land is in unincorporated Cook County,
Commissioner Suffredin agreed to look into the matter for the future.
Commissioner Hansen inquired as to the Ordinance's expected revenue generation.
Barbara Bruno, Director of the Cook County Department of Revenue, responded that $I million to $2
million in new revenue is expected. The additional revenue will result from the increased fees and
enhanced enforcement. Currently, $1 million in revenue is generated annually.
Commissioner Silvestri inquired as to the current fine payment compliance rate.
Ms. Bruno replied approximately 91,000 forms are mailed out each year. Last year approximately 45,000
forms were returned with payment. Hence the compliance rate last year was approximately 50%. Most
of these forms are renewal applications. A second mailing is sent out to those people who do not respond
to the first mailing.
In response to Com missioner Silvestri 's concern regarding the vehicle sticker purchasing compliance rate,
Ms. Bruno suggested that the Department of Revenue could supply the SherifPs Office with a list of
those persons not in compliance.
Commissioner Suffredin noted the Ordinance mm1m1zes administrative costs with regard to senior
citizens. Their stickers currently cost $ 1 and are renewed annuall y. The Substitute Ordinance charges
senior citizens $5 for a vehicle sticker that is valid for as long as that senior citizen owns the vehicle.
Commissioner Silvestri inquired whether vehicle stickers are sold through township offices.
Ms. Bruno replied in the affirmative. She further stated a percentage of the County's revenue is obtained
from township offices. The County supplies township offices with blank applications. Applications
received from the County can be turned in at township offices.
Commissioner Silvestri inquired how the senior citizen stickers will be differentiated from all other
stickers.
Ms. Bruno replied that senior citizen stickers will constitute a distinct class.
Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved to amend Section 13-75(c), by
striking the second sentence, "Each vehicle in violation and each day a violation continues shall
constitute a separate, distinct and chargeable offense separate and apart from any other fees for
purchase of said license(s) or any applicable late fees." The motion to amend carried, and Section
13-75(c) now reads as follows :

requiring a license shall be fined not less than seventy-five dollars

be approved and adopted, as amended. The motion carried.

13-62

License Requirement

It shall be unlawful for any motor vehicle owner residing within the unincorporated area of Cook County
to own, possess, use, or to cause or pennit any of his agents, employees, lessees, or bailees to use any
motor vehicle upon the unincorporated area of Cook County, unless such vehicle be licensed as
hereinafter provided.

13-63

Application

Any person desiring a license for any such motor vehicle or other vehicle shall file an application with the
Bt!rea\f of Aelmisiskatios Department of Revenue (Department) in the Bureau of Finance, upon a form
provided therefor, which shall set forth the name and address of the applicant, a description of the vehicle
for which the license is desired, the place where the same is to be kept when not in use, the number and
kinds of other vehicles kept by the said applicant at such place, and in the case of an application for a
license for a motor vehicle, for what purpose the same is to be used, and such other information as may be
prescribed.

13-64 Exemptions
All vehicles owned and operated upon the public ways of the unincorporated area of Cook County by the
United States Government or any agency thereof, or by the State of Illinois or any department thereof, or
by any political subdivision, public or municipal corporation of the State of Illinois or any department or
other agency of such corporation, or by a nonprofit organization as defined by Section 50 l(c)(3) of the
Internal Revenue Code, as amended, such as the American Red Cross, and all buses owned and operated
by churches in conjunction with the authorized activities of said institutions under Section 3-616 of the
Illinois Vehicle Code, shall be exempt from the vehicle tax. Every exempt vehicle, except those vehicles
owned by the County of Cook which are used by said government agencies in confidential or undercover
investigatory services or by an officer of any said agencies as the officer' s official car shall have the name
of the owner painted in letters at least 1 1/2 inches in length in a conspicuous place on the outside of each
side of the vehicle; provided that in lieu of such identification every vehicle which is exempt from
payment of the state motor vehicle registration fee, shall have a license plate or emblem as provided in
Sections 66 and 67 herein and every vehicle owned by the United States government or any agency
thereof, which is not identified as required in this article, shall have such license plate or emblem. All
license plates or emblems for vehicles exempt from payment of the vehicle tax (a "Z" emblem) shall be
furnished by the Department at no charge.

Issuance
Upon the payment by the applicant of the license fee hereinafter provided, the County shall issue, or
cause to be issued, a license authorizing the use of such vehicle within the unincorporated area of Cook
County.

Motor Bicycle Plate
The Comity Colleetor Department shall deliver to the holder of a license for a motor bicycle, motor
tricycle, or trailer, a metal plate or other license emblem which shall bear the word Cook County and a
number identical with the number of the license the name of the class to which such vehicle belongs and
the year for which such license is issued.

When such metal plate or other license emblem is delivered to the holder of a license for a motor bicycle,
motor tricycle, or trailer, it shall be the duty of such licensee to affix such plate or other license emblem in
a conspicuous position so that the said plate or other license emblem can be easily seen upon the rear end
of such motor bicycle, motor tricycle, or trailer.

Window Sticker
The CouAt)' Colleetor Except for those who receive a sticker under Section 66.1 of this Ordinance, the
Department shall deliver to the holder of any license for any automobile, motor truck, motor ambulance

Removal Upon Sale
Immediately upon the sale of any vehicle licensed under this Ordinance, when such sale is made prior to
the date of expiration of such license, the vendor shall remove the license tag, plate, transparent sticker, or
other license emblem from the vehicle so sold.
Except where a vehicle has been regularly transferred as hereinafter provided in Section 13-71 herein, it
shall be the duty of the purchaser of any used automobile or other vehicle to remove and deliver to the
vendor or the vendor's agent immediately any license tag, plate, transparent sticker or other license
emblem which may be attached to such vehicle at the time of the purchase thereof, when the vendor of
such vehicle may have refused, fai led or omitted to detach from such vehicle as hereinafter required. It
shall be unlawful for any such purchaser to use, sell or offer sale such used automobile or other vehicle
without first having removed all license tags, plates, transparent stickers or other license emblems.

Unlawful Use on Another Vehicle
It shall be unlawful for any person to affix or cause to be affixed any license tag, plate, transparent sticker
or other license emblem to any automobile or other vehicle other than the vehicle to which such license
tag, plate, transparent sticker or other license emblem was intended to be affixed at the time of the
issuance thereof by the CouAt)' Collector Department.

270

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005

Transfer
Whenever the owner of any vehicle licensed under this Ordinance, before the expiration of such license,
sells or otherwise disposes of such vehicle, and thereafter acquires another vehicle and desires to transfer
the vehicle license originally issued for the vehicle disposed of to such newly-acquired vehicle, such
owner shall immediately make application to the Cotmty Golleetor Department for a transfer of said
vehicle license to the newly-purchased vehicle. Said application shall state the name and address of the
licensee and the name and address of the purchaser of said vehicle, together with a description of the
newly-purchased vehicle. Upon surrender of the original license and transparent sticker or vehicle tag in
case a metal tag has been issued, or upon proof that the transparent sticker or plate has been destroyed, the
Couaty Colleetor Department shall transfer said license to apply to the new-acquired vehicle upon
payment of the proper license fee of $10.00, provided, that the Cotiaty Collector Department shall not
transfer any license where the transparent sticker emblem issued under said license is defaced or
mutilated so as to prevent identification of the emblem. It shall be unlawful for any person to displace a
transparent sticker emblem on any vehicle other than the vehicle for which the emblem was originally
issued, without first transferring the license to such other vehicle, as provided herein.
The owner of any vehicle licensed under this Ordinance shall promptly notify the Gotiaty Collector
Department aaa the Sheriff whenever the transparent sticker emblem issued under such license is lost,
stolen or destroyed. A duplicate transparent sticker may be purchased from the Department for $20.00.

Dealer License

If any manufacturer or dealer ffi of any of the motor vehicles mentioned in this Ordinance shall make
application to the Cotiaty Golleetor Department and shall state that he the manufacturer or dealer is a
manufacturer operating a plant for the construction of motor vehicles within the unincorporated area of
Cook County, or a dealer in such motor vehicles with a salesroom located within the unincorporated area
of Cook County~ and ~ desires a license emblem to be used by lHm the dealer or +t manufacturer, the
Cotiaty Collector Department shall upon payment by such applicant of the fee hereinafter set for to such
manufacturer or dealer a distinctive license plate or transparent sticker license emblem with a number
thereon. Said emblem must be attached to or borne by any such motor vehicles while being operated on
the streets of the unincorporated area of Cook County. When any such vehicle is in use and carries such
license plate or transparent sticker license emblem, no other license fee shall be collected under the
provision of the this ordinance.
The annual license fee to be paid for each such license plate or transparent sticker license emblem shall be
$20.00, and said fee shall not be prorated.

Business Vehicle Identification
It shall be unlawful for any person to use or to cause or pennit any of his a person's employees to use any
motor vehicle, or other vehicle~ in the transportation of property upon the public ways of the
unincorporated area of Cook County unless such vehicle shall have the name and address of the owner
thereof, and a serial number distinguishing said vehicle from any other vehicle controlled or used by the
same person plainly painted, in the letters at least one and one-half inches in length, in a conspicuous
place on the outside of such vehicle, provided that any such person using and operating in the
unincorporated area of Cook County more than five such vehicles may cause such name and serial
number to be painted on each vehicle as foresaid in letter not less than three inches in length and omit
therefrom the address of such person~ Qrovided, further, that in event if such vehicle is used or operated
continuously by a Jessee or bailee or other person having complete control over such vehicle, instead of
the owner thereof, the name and address and serial number or name and serial number, as the case may
be, of such lessee, bailee or other person using and operating said vehicle may be used as if the person
were the owner thereof. Such name, address and serial number, or name and serial number, as the case
may be, shall be kept so painted, plainly and distinctly, at all times while such vehicle is in use on the
public ways of the unincorporated area of Cook County. This section shall not be construed as applying to
street ears ninAiRg OR metallie rails, or to any motor vehicle, or other vehicle which is used exclusively
for pleasure non commercial purposes.

13-75

Penalty for Ordinance Violation

(a) Late Fee
Any person or motor vehicle as defined in 13-61 or 13-62 who purchases a license after the effective day
shall pay a late fee penalty equal to the amount due for the license fee but not less than twenty-five dollars
($25.00) per license whichever is more. Persons over Age Sixty-Five, physically handicapped individuals
or disabled veterans shall not be charged more than $25.00 for a late fee.
(b) Back dated fees

Any person or motor vehicle as defined in 13-61 or 13-62 who did not purchase a license after the
effective date may be required to pay the entire amount of fees due for each of the prior three years that
the fee had not been paid.
(c) Penalty for Failure to Properly Display Sticker
Any owner, driver or motor vehicle in violation of these provisions requiring a license shall be fined not
less than seventy-five dollars ($75.00) per offense nor more than one hundred fifty ($150) per offense.
