271504

AMENDMENT TO THE COOK COUNTY PURCHASING ACT (AMENDED
PROPOSED RESOLUTION). Submitting an Amended Proposed Resolution sponsored
by John P. Daley, County Commissioner; Co-Sponsored by Anthony J. Peraica and Peter
N. Silvestri, County Commissioners.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Purchasing Agent of Cook County is charged with the responsibility of
soliciting bids and entering into contracts for commodities and services as specified by all
Cook County agencies; and
WHEREAS, the Office of the Cook County Purchasing Agent strives to serve the
citizens of the County of Cook through the use of sound, prudent, and consistent
procurement practices for those departments and agencies which report to the President
and the Cook County Board of Commissioners; and
WHEREAS, the Office of the Cook County Purchasing Agent is committed to fulfilling
the needs of Cook County agencies in an environment in which vendors receive fair and
impartial treatment in doing business with Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the Office of the Cook County Purchasing Agent, in addition to other
bureaus, departments, and agencies of Cook County, may determine that contracts for
certain commodities and services are appropriate for procurement under terms outlined in
the issuance of a Request for Proposal, commonly referred to as an " RFP"; and
WHEREAS, the technical and detailed nature of the process for development of an
effective RFP may in certain cases require assistance, advice, or oversight from
professional consultants who are compensated accordingly for their work product; and
WHEREAS, in such cases, a conflict of interest may exist in the event that a professional
consultant, acting as either an individual or business entity and party to a contractual
relationship with Cook County, under terms providing for services related to the
preparation of an RFP, subsequently seeks to be awarded additional business with Cook
County in the performance of duties or provision of goods and/or services as described in
the RFP; and
WHEREAS, among purchasing professionals in both the private and public sectors,
commonly known best practices in the industry are specifically designed to prevent such
conflicts of interest when the purchaser is acquiring goods and services under the aegis of
an RFP process; now, therefore
BE IT RESOLVED, by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County that the Board
does hereby amend the Cook County Purchasing Act to incorporate these industry best
practices, and to prohibit the awarding of contracts for goods and/or services to any
individual or business entity under the tenns of a Request for Proposal, when said
individual or business entity was directly and substantially involved in drafting, writing,
researching or preparing the RFP and any ancillary documents related to same; and

275

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this amendment to the Cook County Purchasing
Act is immediately effective upon becoming law.
*Referred to the Committee on Finance on 06/07/05.
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved to receive and file
Communication No. 271504. The motion carried.
274516

PRECINCT ASSISTANTS FOR 2006 ELECTIONS - PILOT PROGRAM (PROPOSED
ORDINANCE). Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by Larry Suffredin, Bobbie
L. Steele and Peter N. Silvestri, County Commissioners; Co-Sponsored by Joan Patricia
Murphy, County Commissioner.
The following is a synopsis of the Proposed Ordinance:
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, conducting fair and impartial elections is one of the most important
functions of government to insure confidence in the democratic process; and
WHEREAS, the County of Cook often faces shortages of election workers with
technological skills on Election Day; and
WHEREAS, recruiting reliable Precinct Assistants who can devote Election Day to
assisting judges in technical trouble-shooting and setting up equipment is essential to the
integrity of the electoral process; and
WHEREAS, such temporary assignments have had a favorable impact on the election
process.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED THAT:
the County of Cook, in conjunction with the Cook County Clerk's Office, wi ll
undertake a pilot program to recruit, train and assign 100 employees of Cook County
from selected offices of County officials to serve as Precinct Assistants on Election Day
in suburban Cook County. The pilot program will be in effect for the elections on March
2 1 and November 7, 2006.

(I)

(2)
Cook County employees who choose to participate in the pilot program will be
excused from their regular work assignment with the pennission of the chief executive of
their department, agency or bureau to attend a mandatory two hour training workshop.
On Election Day these previously trained county employees will be excused from their
regular work assignment with the pennission of the chief executive of their department,
agency or bureau to assist with Election Day activities in suburban Cook County. They
will serve as Precinct Assistants to ensure that all polling places are operated efficiently
and accurately. These employees will receive a one-time stipend, the amount depending
on specific work assignments, in addition to their nonnal day' s pay.
(3)
The Cook County Clerk's Office and the President's Office will implement this
pilot program.
*Referred to the Committee on Finance on 12/06/05.
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved to accept the Substitute
Ordinance for Communication No. 274516. The motion carried.

276

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

SUBSTITUTE ORDINANCE FOR COMMUNICATION NO. 274516
PROPOSED ORDINANCE CREATING A PILOT
COOK COUNTY ELECTION TECHNICAL ASSISTANT PROGRAM
WHEREAS, conducting fair and impartial elections is one of the most important
functions of government to insure confidence in and the integrity of the democratic
process; and
WHEREAS, elections within Cook County, excluding that portion of those elections
which is conducted within the City of Chicago, ("suburban elections") are the
responsibility of the Cook County Clerk; and
WHEREAS, suburban elections are conducted at polling places for each election
precinct which are under the supervision of Election Judges appointed by the Cook
County Clerk; and
WHEREAS, in accordance with the federal Help America Vote Act ("HA VA"), the
Cook County Clerk is implementing new voting equipment ("System") beginning with
the March 21, 2006 primary election, which System will replace the punch card system
which has been in use during suburban elections for many years; and
WHEREAS, the new System will include several new types of equipment which
represent the latest in election technology and which will be easier for voters to use; and
WHEREAS, in order to ensure a smooth transition to the new System, it is critical that
reliable and qualified personnel be trained and available in the precinct polling places to
set up and operate the new System equipment; and
WHEREAS, even in previous suburban elections using the older punch card voting
equipment, the Cook County Clerk has experienced difficulties in identifying and training
a sufficient number of workers with technological skills to assist on election day; and
WHEREAS, the Clerk, the President and the Board have identified a cost effective and
reliable solution to deploy trained technical assistants to provide technical troubleshooting and equipment set up assistance on behalf of the Clerk on election day and
desire to implement this solution on a pilot basis.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED THAT:
( 1)
Pilot Program Established. The County of Cook, in conjunction with
the Cook County Clerk's Office and the Board President's Office and with the
voluntary cooperation of the elected officials comprising County government,
will undertake a pilot program to recruit, train and assign 100 employees working
within Cook County government to serve as technical assistants for the March
21, 2006 primary and the November 7, 2006 General Election.

277

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005

(2)

Compensation and T raining of Technical Assistants. Cook County employees
who qualify for, are selected and agree to participate as technical assistants in the
pilot program will be excused from their regular work assignments with the
pennission of the chief executive of their department, agency or bureau to attend
a mandatory two-hour training workshop. If they successfully complete this
training workshop, technical assistants shall also be excused from their regular
work assignment with the permission of the chief executive of their department,
agency or bureau on Election Day to provide technical assistance in suburban
Cook County. In addition to their regular salaries, these election assistants will
receive either overtime pay or a stipend payment, the amount of which shall
depend on the specific work assignment, to compensate them for h ours worked
beyond a normal eight hour day for each suburban election worked.

(3)

Implementation. The Cook County Clerk's office, the President's Office and
the Cook County elected officials who voluntarily participate in this pilot
program shall enter into an interagency agreement setting forth the details of their
participation in the program for each election.

(4)

Effective Date. This Ordinance shall go into effect immediately upon passage
by the Board of Commissioners.

Chairman Daley inquired whether funds for this program are currently available to the Clerk's Office.
Brandon Neese, Deputy County Clerk, replied in the affinnative. He specified that funds are available in
the 120 Account (Overtime), and in the 133 Account (Per D iem). He noted that the latter account is used
specifically for election-day employees. He further noted that there should be sufficient funds allocated
for these accounts.
Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved to amend the Substitute
Ordinance by inserting at the end of sub-point (2), the following: "Such compensation shall be paid
only from funds available to the Clerk of Cook County". The motion to amend carried.
Commissioner Peraica inquired as to the timing of the implementation of the Ordinance and the purpose
of the technical election assistants.
Mr. Neese replied that the County is converting to more technically sophisticated equipment, namely,
optical scan and touch screen. Also this is the first equipment change in 25-27 years. For both of these
reasons, there will be a learning curve for all involved. While the County has used technical election
assistants since 2000, the new equipment will require more extensive assistance, in terms of set-up, usage
and procedures. Other large counties and some states have converted to this equipment, and the Clerk' s
Office has reviewed their usage of technical election assistants. Ohio, for example, uses all of its
employees on election days. This is also true of Clark County, Nevada. The expected need for Cook
County is one assistant per every two polling places.
Commissioner Peraica inquired whether this Ordinance applies only to suburban Cook County.
Mr. Neese replied in the affirmative.
Commissioner Peraica inquired how long Cook County has utilized technical election assistants.

278

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

Mr. Neese replied that the City has used them since at least 2000 and that Cook County has used them for
at least this long.
Commissioner Peraica inquired what scope of training the technical election assistants will receive.
Mr. Neese defined this scope as setting up and starting equipment, trouble shooting and assisting the
12,000 election judges. Some of these judges possess no technical skills.
Mr. Neese assured Commissioner Peraica that the issue of electioneering has been addressed m
discussions between the Clerk's Office and the State' s Attorney's Office.
Michael Prinzi, Assistant State's Attorney, State's Attorney's Office, further addressed Commissioner
Peraica's concern regarding electioneering. He stated there is a good faith component involved, however,
the Clerk's Office will make explicit the constraints of the election Jaw, during the training of the
technical election assistants.
Commissioner Peraica inquired from which pay grade levels the assistants will be drawn.
Mr. Neese replied that there is no targeted pay grade, however, the Clerk's Office is seeking employees
with technical aptitude. The technical election assistants must successfully complete training and pass an
exam. Because this is a pilot program, only 100 County employees are being used.
Commissioner Peraica inquired whether the technical election assistants will earn overtime pay consistent
with their pay grade.
Mr. Neese replied in the affirmative.
Commissioner Peraica inquired how long it will take to compute the votes.
Mr. Neese replied that the Clerk's Office, in conjunction with Sequoia Voting Systems, Inc. , is currently
performing a dry run of the election; the Clerk's Office will provide the results to the Commissioners.
The computing time varies among polling places depending upon the type of ballots cast; nursing home
ballots and absentee ballots in particular require more time to process.
Commissioner Peraica inquired how early votes are handled in the computing process.
Mr. Neese replied that early ballots must be cast through the optical scan system on paper ballots at one of
the approximately 100 municipal voting sites. Under current law, these ballots must be forwarded to the
polling places for counting. There is pending legislation, initiated collectively by all Illinois clerks, to
instead forward early votes to one centralized location. This legislation is scheduled to be considered in
January, and the Commissioners will be kept abreast of any changes in the law.
Commissioner Collins stated that she thought it would have been more effective to recruit technical
election assistants from elsewhere than among Cook County employees, particularly from area colleges.
Mr. Neese replied that the Clerk's Office has recruited technical election assistants not only from area
colleges, but also from high schools, the League of Women Voters and the private sector, including Sears,
Coldwell Banker (which is supplying 100 technical election assistants) and other banks. There will be
more high school and college students involved this year, and they will receive academic credit for their
work.

279

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

Commissioner Hansen inquired as to the ratio of technical election assistants to polling places.
Mr. Neese replied that the ratio is approximately one technical election assistant per two polling places.
Commissioner Hansen inquired as to who selects the technical election assistants.
Mr. Neese replied that the Office of the Clerk makes all of the selections.
Commissioner Hansen voiced his fear that the technical election assistants might electioneer at the polling
places. He inquired whether the technical election assistants will have any judicial responsibility.
Mr. Neese replied that in no way do the technical election assistants supersede the statutory and legal
responsibility of the judges. They are merely agents of the Clerk. The judges have the authority to
remove any technical election assistant. The judges will be instructed as to the role of technical election
assistants. Mr. Neese reiterated that the technical election assistants will be strictly instructed that they
must remain non-partisan while discharging their duties.
Commissioner Hansen inquired whether a tape of the voting, including early voting, could be available at
each polling place at the time of the poll's closing.
Mr. Neese replied in the negative. He stated that the early voting results could be obtained fifteen
minutes after the election ends on the Clerk' s Office website.
Commissioner Maldonado inquired who receives the stipend mentioned in the Ordinance.
Mr. Neese replied that stipends are awarded to Cook County employees who work more than eight hours
per day but who are not entitled to overtime pay in their pennanent position.
Commissioner Maldonado inquired how much the stipend is and whether all stipends are the same
amount.
Mr. Neese stated that the stipend amount has not yet been detennined, but that it will be approximately
$250.
Commissioner Maldonado noted that the technical election assistants would almost certainly work
overtime, given that they would be required to be at the polling places before and after the voting; this
would total approximately 14 hours. He asked for clarification regarding how technical election
assistants could move back and forth between polling places after the polls are closed.
Mr. Neese stated that the technical election assistants, as agents of the County Clerk, are authorized to
leave and re-enter polling places after they are closed.
Commissioner Hansen asked for further clarification of the current statute as it pertains to where early
votes are counted.
Mr. Neese replied that under the current statute, touch screen votes are counted centrally and optical scan
votes are counted in each individual precinct.

280

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005

Chairman Daley raised the concern that election judges are required to use vacation or personal time to
serve in their capacity, and that it is inconsistent that County employees who are working as technical
election assistants are not required to use vacation or personal time and, further, some technical election
assistants receive stipends, which amount to pay above and beyond what they are usually entitled to.
Shalom Gliksman, Budget Analyst, Department of Budget Management Services, stated that funds are
available in Fund 524-129 (Seasonal) and Fund 524-133 (Per Diem).
Chairman Daley clarified that the 524 fund pertains to elections.
Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Claypool, moved to amend the Substitute
Ordinance by further amending sub-point (2), as follows: "Such compensation shall be paid only
from funds available to the Clerk of Cook County in Funds 524-129 (Seasonal Employees) or 524133 (Per Diem Employees). The motion to amend carried.
Commissioner Silvestri requested that Mr. Neese clarify the purpose of the stipends.
Mr. Neese replied that a stipend provides compensation for any work perfonned beyond eight hours on
election day by eligible technical election assistants. The technical election assistants who are eligible for
stipends are those Cook County employees who are salaried and who therefore are not entitled to
overtime pay in the course of their permanent positions with the County or in their capacity as technical
election assistants .
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the Substitute Ordinance
(Communication No. 274516) be approved and adopted, as amended. The motion carried.
06-0-03
ORDINANCE

ORDINANCE CREATING A PILOT
COOK COUNTY ELECTION TECHNICAL ASSISTANT PROGRAM
WHEREAS, conducting fair and impartial elections is one of the most important functions of
government to insure confidence in and the integrity of the democratic process; and
WHEREAS, elections within Cook County, excluding that portion of those elections which is conducted
within the City of Chicago, ("suburban elections") are the responsibility of the Cook County Clerk; and
WHEREAS, suburban elections are conducted at polling places for each election precinct which are
under the supervision of Election Judges appointed by the Cook County Clerk; and
WHEREAS, in accordance with the federal Help America Vote Act ("HA VA" ), the Cook County Clerk
is implementing new voting equipment ("System") beginning with the March 21 , 2006 primary election,
which System will replace the punch card system which has been in use during suburban elections for
many years; and
WHEREAS, the new System will include several new types of equipment which represent the latest in
election technology and which will be easier for voters to use; and

281

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005

WHEREAS, in order to ensure a smooth transition to the new System, it is critical that reliable and
qualified personnel be trained and available in the precinct polling places to set up and operate the new
System equipment; and
WHEREAS, even in previous suburban elections using the older punch card voting equipment, the Cook
County Clerk has experienced difficulties in identifying and training a sufficient number of workers with
technological skills to assist on election day; and
WHEREAS, the Clerk, the President and the Board have identified a cost effective and reliable solution
to deploy trained technical assistants to provide technical trouble-shooting and equipment set up
assistance on behalf of the Clerk on election day and desire to implement this solution on a pilot basis.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED THAT:
(!)

Pilot Program Established. The County of Cook, in conjunction with the Cook County Clerk ' s
Office and the Board President' s Office and with the voluntary cooperation of the elected
officials comprising County government, will undertake a pilot program to recruit, train and
assign I00 employees working within Cook County government to serve as technical assistants
for the March 21 , 2006 primary and the November 7, 2006 General Election.

(2)

Compensation and Training of Technical Assistants. Cook County employees who qualify
for, are selected and agree to participate as technical assistants in the pilot program will be
excused from their regular work assignments with the permission of the chief executive of their
department, agency or bureau to attend a mandatory two-hour training workshop. If they
successfully complete this training workshop, technical assistants shall also be excused from their
regular work assignment with the permission of the chief executive of their department, agency
or bureau on Election Day to provide technical assistance in suburban Cook County. In addition
to their regular salaries, these election assistants will receive either overtime pay or a stipend
payment, the amount of which shall depend on the specific work assignment, to compensate them
for hours worked beyond a normal eight hour day for each suburban election worked. Such
compensation shall be paid only from funds available to the Clerk of Cook County in funds 524129 Seasonal Employees or 524-133 Per Diem Employees.

(3)

Implementation. The Cook County Clerk' s office, the President' s Office and the Cook County
elected officials who voluntarily participate in this pilot program shall enter into an interagency
agreement setting forth the details of their participation in the program for each election .

(4)

Effective Date. This Ordinance shall go into effect immediately upon passage by the Board of
Commissioners.

Approved and adopted this 2 lst day of December 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

274519

ORDINANCE AMENDING CHAPTER 10:
THE CONTRACTING AND
PURCHASING ORDINANCE OF COOK COUNTY (PROPOSED ORDINANCE
AMENDMENT). Submitting a Proposed Ordinance Amendment sponsored by John P.
Daley, County Commissioner; Co-Sponsored by Anthony J. Peraica, Peter N. Silvestri,
Jerry Butler, Forrest Claypool, Earlean Collins, Elizabeth Ann Doody Gorman, Carl R.
Hansen, Roberto Maldonado, Joseph Mario Moreno, Joan Patricia Mumhy, Deborah
Sims, Bobbie L. Steele and Larry Suffredin, County Commissioners.
PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT
WHEREAS, the Purchasing Agent of Cook County is charged with the responsibility of
soliciting bids and entering into contracts for commodities and services as specified by all
Cook County agencies; and
WHEREAS, the office of the Cook County Purchasing Agent strives to serve the citizens
of the County of Cook through the use of sound, prudent, and consistent procurement
practices for those departments and agencies which report to the President and Cook
County Board of Commissioners; and
WHEREAS, the office of the Cook County Purchasing Agent is committed to fulfilling
the needs of Cook County agencies in an environment in which vendors receive fair and
impartial treatment in doing business with Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the office of the Cook County Purchasing Agent, in addition to other
bureaus, departments, and agencies of Cook County, may determine that contracts for
certain commodities and services are appropriate for procurement under tenns outlined in
the issuance of a Request for Proposal, commonly referred to as an "RFP"; and
WHEREAS, the technical and detailed nature of the process for development of an
effective RFP may in certain cases require assistance, advice, or oversight from
professional consultants who are compensated accordingly for their work product; and
WHEREAS, in such cases, a conflict of interest may exist in the event that a professional
consultant, acting as either an individual or business entity and party to a contractual
relationship with Cook County, under terms providing for services related to the
preparation of an RFP, subsequently seeks to be awarded additional business with Cook
County in the performance of duties or provision of goods and/or services as described in
the RFP; and
WHEREAS, among purchasing professionals in both the private and public sectors,
commonly known best practices in the industry are specifically designed to prevent such
conflicts of interest when the purchaser is acquiring goods and services under the aegis of
an RFP process; now, therefore
BE IT ORDAINED by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County that the Board does
hereby amend Section I 9 of Chapter 10 (Contracting and Purchasing Ordinance of Cook
County) to incorporate these industry best practices, and to prohibit the awarding of
contracts for goods and/or services to any individual or business entity under the terms of
a Request For Proposal, when said individual or business entity was directly and
substantially involved in drafting, writing, researching or preparing the RFP and any
ancillary documents related to same, to wit:

283

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

Section 1. Section 19 of Chapter I 0 is hereby amended to add the following:
Award of Contracts Not Adaptable to Competitive Bidding
I 0-19. Contracts which by their nature are not adapted to award by competitive biddings,
such as contracts for the services of individuals possessing a high degree of professional
skill where the ability or fitness of the individual plays an important part, contracts for
printing of Finance Committee pamphlets, Comptroller's estimates, and departmental
reports, contracts for the printing or engraving of bonds, tax warrants, and other evidence
of indebtedness, contracts for utility services such as heat, light, water, telephone, or
telegraph, and contracts for the purchase of books, magazines, periodicals, and other
similar articles of an educational or instructional nature, and the binding of such books,
magazines, periodicals, pamphlets, reports, or similar articles shall not be subject to the
competitive bidding requirements of this ordinance. The Purchasing Agent is expressly
authorized to procure from any Federal, State, or local government unit or agency thereof
such surplus materials, supplies, commodities, or equipment as may be made available
through the operation of any legislation heretofore or hereinafter enacted without
conforming to the competitive bidding requirements of this ordinance. Regular
employment contracts in the County service, whether with respect to the classified
services or otherwise, shall not be subject to the provisions of this ordinance, nor shall
this ordinance be applicable to the granting or issuance pursuant to powers conferred by
laws, ordinances, or resolutions, or franchises, licenses, permits, or other authorizations
by the County Board, or by departments, offices, institutions, boards, commissions,
agencies, or other instrumentalities of the County, nor to contracts or transactions, other
than the sale or lease of personal property pursuant to which the County is the recipient of
money. (Ord. adopted Feb 20, 1973, amend. Oct. 20, 1975 , p. 547 1; July 7, 1980,
p.6078)
In addition to the specific exemptions from the competitive bidding process contained in
Section I 0-19, there are certain contracts which may be more advantageously or
practicably procured through the development and issuance of a request for proposal,
commonly referred to as an "RFP". The development of an effective RFP pursuant to
Chapter I0, or the development of competitive bid documents pursuant to the provisions
of Section 10-18, may in some cases involve the retention of professional consultants
who are compensated for their work product. In such cases, a conflict of interest may
arise in the event said professional consultant, acting either as an individual or as part of
the same or another business entity, subsequently participates in the preparation of a
proposal or bid which is submitted in response to the competitive bid or RFP at issue.
These professional consultants shall be prohibited from participating in the preparation of
a proposal or bid which is submitted in response to the RFP or bid documents where the
professional consultant participated in the development of the RFP or bid documents.
The Purchasing Agent shall have the authority to adopt procedures and promulgate rules
with respect to this section, and
Section 2. This amendment to Chapter I 0 of the Ordinances of Cook County 1s
immediately effective upon becoming law.
*Referred to the Committee on Finance on 12/06/05.

284

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005
Commissioners Silvestri and Maldonado commented that this Ordinance is a positive change to the
purchasing process.
Chairman Daley stated that if a vendor is part of the process of developing an RFP, that vendor is
precluded from submitting a bid on the contract.
Commissioner Maldonado asked leave that all members be added as co-sponsors.
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved that the Ordinance
(Communication No. 274519) be approved and adopted. The motion carried.

ORDINANCE

Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN P. DALEY, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE ANTHONY J. PERAICA, PETER N. SILVESTRI,
JERRY BUT LER, FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS,
ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, CARL R. HANSEN, ROBERTO MALDONADO,
JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, DEBORAH SIMS,
BOBBIE L. STEELE AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS

AMENDMENT TO THE CONTRACTING AND PURCHASING
ORDINANCE OF COOK COUNTY, CHAPTER 10
WHEREAS, the Purchasing Agent of Cook County is charged with the responsibility of soliciting bids
and entering into contracts for commodities and services as specified by all Cook County agencies; and
WHEREAS, the office of the Cook County Purchasing Agent strives to serve the citizens of the County
of Cook through the use of sound, prudent, and consistent procurement practices for those departments
and agencies which report to the President and Cook County Board of Commissioners; and
WHEREAS, the office of the Cook County Purchasing Agent is committed to fulfilling the needs of
Cook County agencies in an environment in which vendors receive fair and impartial treatment in doing
business with Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the office of the Cook County Purchasing Agent, in addition to other bureaus, departments,
and agencies of Cook County, may determine that contracts for certain commodities and services are
appropriate for procurement under terms outlined in the issuance of a Request for Proposal, commonly
referred to as an "RFP"; and
WHEREAS, the technical and detailed nature of the process for development of an effective RFP may in
certain cases require assistance, advice, or oversight from professional consultants who are compensated
accordingly for their work product; and

285

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005

WHEREAS, in such cases, a conflict of interest may exist in the event that a professional consultant,
acting as either an individual or business entity and party to a contractual relationship with Cook County,
under tenns providing for services related to the preparation of an RFP, subsequently seeks to be awarded
additional business with Cook County in the perfonnance of duties or provision of goods and/or services
as described in the RFP; and
WHEREAS, among purchasing professionals in both the private and public sectors, commonly known
best practices in the industry are specifically designed to prevent such conflicts of interest when the
purchaser is acquiring goods and services under the aegis of an RFP process; now, therefore,
BE IT ORDAINED, by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County that the Board does hereby amend
Section 19 of Chapter 10 (Contracting and Purchasing) of the Cook County Purchasing Act to incorporate
these industry best practices, and to prohibit the awarding of contracts for goods and/or services to any
individual or business entity under the tenns of a Request For Proposal , when said individual or business
entity was directly and substantially involved in drafting, writing, researching or preparing the RFP and
any ancillary documents related to same, to wit:
Section 1. Section 19 of Chapter I 0 is hereby amended to add the following:
Award of Contracts Not Adaptable to Competitive Bidding
10-19. Contracts which by their nature are not adapted to award by competitive biddings, such as
contracts for the services of individuals possessing a high degree of professional skill where the ability or
fitness of the individual plays an important part, contracts for printing of Finance Committee pamphlets,
Comptroller's estimates, and departmental reports, contracts for the printing or engraving of bonds, tax
warrants, and other evidence of indebtedness, contracts for utility services such as heat, light, water,
telephone, or telegraph, and contracts for the purchase of books, magazines, periodicals, and other similar
articles of an educational or instructional nature, and the binding of such books, magazines, periodicals,
pamphlets, reports, or similar articles shall not be subject to the competitive bidding requirements of this
ordinance. The Purchasing Agent is expressly authorized to procure from any Federal, State, or local
government unit or agency thereof such surplus materials, supplies, commodities, or equipment as may be
made available through the operation of any legislation heretofore or hereinafter enacted without
confonning to the competitive bidding requirements of this ordinance. Regular employment contracts in
the County service, whether with respect to the classified services or otherwise, shall not be subject to the
provisions of this ordinance, nor shall this ordinance be applicable to the granting or issuance pursuant to
powers conferred by laws, ordinances, or resolutions, or franchises, licenses, permits, or other
authorizations by the County Board, or by departments, offices, institutions, boards, commissions,
agencies, or other instrumentalities of the County, nor to contracts or transactions, other than the sale or
lease of personal property pursuant to which the County is the recipient of money. (Ord. adopted Feb 20,
1973, amend. Oct. 20, 1975, p. 5471 ; July 7, 1980, p.6078)
In addition to the specific exemptions from the competitive bidding process contained in Section I 0-19,
there are certain contracts which may be more advantageously or practicably procured through the
development and issuance of a request for proposal, commonly referred to as an " RFP" . The development
of an effective RFP pursuant to Chapter 10, or the development of competitive bid documents pursuant to
the provisions of Section 10-1 8, may in some cases involve the retention of professional consultants who
are compensated for their work product. In such cases, a conflict of interest may arise in the event said
professional consultant, acting either as an individual or as part of the same or another business entity,
subsequently participates in the preparation of a proposal or bid which is submitted in response to the
competitive bid or RFP at issue.

286

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005
These professional consultants shall be prohibited from participating in the preparation of a proposal or
bid which is submitted in response to the RFP or bid documents where the professional consultant
participated in the development of the RFP or bid documents.
The Purchasing Agent shall have the authority to adopt procedures and promulgate rules with respect to
this Section.

Section 2. This amendment to Chapter l 0 of the Ordinances of Cook County is immediately effective
upon becoming law.
Approved and adopted this 21st day of December 2005.

STA TE'S ATTORNEY, Richard A. Devine, submitting communication advising the
County to resolve a matter brought against the County by the Illinois Environmental
Protection Agency ("!EPA") Permit Investigation Violation Notice 2003-00273. This
matter involved the alleged failure to satisfy certain pennitting and reporting
requirements. On December 7, 2005 the Finance Committee' s Subcommittee on
Litigation recommended the following settlement.
The State has offered to settle the alleged violations without the payment of monetary
penalties to the State. Rather, pursuant to the settlement offered by the State, the County
will perform a Supplemental Environmental Project ("SEP") to increase energy
efficiency at a building owned by the County at a cost of $25,000.00. This project will be
paid for under a County Capital Improvement Program.
Additionally, it is the County's contention that some of the alleged violations resulted
from acts or omissions of the County's contractors. The contractors have offered a total
of $30,000.00 to offset expenses of the County. We respectfully request authorization for
the County to enter into a settlement agreement with the contractors for a total of not less
than $30,000.00 to be paid by the contractors to the County.

274514

HARRIS & HARRIS (PROPOSED CONTRACT) FOR COLLECTION SERVICES
FOR DELINQUENT TRAFFIC FINES AND FEES. Transmitting a Communication,
dated November 17, 2005 from Dorothy Brown, Clerk of the Circuit Court:
I am writing to inform you of an initiative for which I would appreciate your
consideration and support at the December 6, 2005 Board Meeting.
Specifically, I would like to request authorization from the Cook County Board of
Commissioners for the Office of the Clerk of the Circuit Court to engage the firm of
Harris & Harris for a two year period to perform accounts receivable collection services
for delinquent fines and fees due and owing to the Clerk' s Office. The goals of this
initiative are to collect as much revenue as possible and to bring past due accounts that
are deemed uncollectible by an independent qualified finn to closure.
The collection services provided by Harris & Harris will be performed on a competitive
basis with no cost to Cook County. All fees associated with the collection of a past due
fine or fee will be added in addition to the fine or fee amount as permitted by Illinois
Public Act 093-0836, which became law in 2004.
The scope of the collection services that Harris & Harris would be engaged to perfonn
would concentrate solely on past due Traffic fines and fees.
The horizon of time that will be addressed for the collection of past due fines and fees
will span in excess of ten ( l 0) years.

321

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005

Established in 1968, Harris & Harris has the resources necessary to perfonn collection
services for a court system the size of the Circuit Court of Cook County efficiently and
effectively, using state-of-the art technology as well as industry standard collection
procedures. The decision to select Harris & Harris for this engagement was predicated
on a due diligence review perfonned by the Clerk of the Circuit Court of several finns
who presented their services for consideration.

*Referred to the Finance Committee on December 6, 2005.

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Business and Economic Development of the Board of Commissioners of Cook
County met pursuant to notice on Monday, December 19, 2005 at the hour of I0:00 A.M. in the Board
Room, Room 569, County Building, 118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Committee has considered the following item and upon adoption of this report, the recommendation
is as follows:
274513

DEPARTMENT OF PLANNING AND DEVELOPMENT, by Peter Nicholson, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated November 16, 2005:
Re:

HOME Investment Partnerships Program (HOME Program)

respectfully request approval of a HOME Investment Partnerships Program (HOME
Program) Loan in the amount of $1,500,000.00.
Cook County has received a request totaling $1,500,000.00 in HOME funds from Cook
County Housing Development Corporation, d/b/a Turnstone Development, for the
construction of 70 units of senior independent rental apartments in the Village of Calumet
Park. The subject site is located just south of the comer of l 24th and Morgan Streets in
Calumet Park, Cook County, Illinois.
The Village of Calumet Park approached Turnstone Development and requested they
build 70 units of senior independent rental apartments in the Village of Calumet Park.
The Village has made several commitments to the project, including the creation of a
single purpose TIF for this project, donation of 2.9 acres of land, approximately
$700,000.00 in bond proceeds, other TIF revenues, as available, and the forgiveness of
building pennits. These commitments will be supplemented by 1st mortgage financing
from HOME funds from IHDA, Cook County, and Low Income Housing Tax Credits.
The proposed budget is estimated at $11,614,798.00 which includes all construction and
soft costs associated with the development. The HOME loan of $1,500,000.00 accounts
for 12.9% of the estimated project costs and represents an investment of $42,857.00 per
HOME unit in the development.

331

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 2 1, 2005

The terms of the HOME Program loan will be structured as a 40-year amortization period
at 1% interest. The County HOME Program will receive annual principal and interest
payments of $45,514.00 to be used for other HOME eligible activities.
I respectfully request approval of this project, and that the Chief Administrative Officer
of the County of Cook, or his designee, authorize execution on behalf of the County of
Cook, any and all documents necessary to further the project approved herein, including
but not limited to the HOME Loan agreement and any modifications thereto. The
approval of this loan by this Honorable Body will pennit staff to issue necessary
commitments to allow this project to move forward.
Fiscal Impact: None. Grant funds: $ 1,500,000.00. (772-298 Account).
*Referred to the Committee on Business and Economic Development on 12/06/05.
Commissioner Murphy, seconded by Commissioner
Communication No. 274513. The motion carried.

Michael E. LaMont - Director, Office of Capital Planning and Policy; and Al Riley Planner, Office of Capital Planning and Policy

332

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Construction of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant to notice
on Wednesday, December 14, 2005 at the hour of 9:30 A.M. in the Board Room, Room 569, County
Building, 118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Committee has considered the following items and, upon adoption of this report, the
recommendations are as follows:
274495

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated November 17, 2005:
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for the Purchasing Agent to advertise
for bids for the Hawthorne Warehouse Renovation, Phase 1 Roof Replacement. It is
respectfully requested that this Honorable Body approve this request.
Reason:

This project phase provides for the tear off and replacement of approximately
413,000 square feet of deteriorated roof. The site is a multi-level facility
comprised of 22 different roof areas of varying size. The work is to include
the removal of all unused, obsolete, and abandoned equipment from the roof
and all associated structural restoration, and repairs of deteriorated parapet
walls and broken masonry. The roof is of an undetermined age and is
showing signs of leakage and damage. This work will provide for a safe and
dry environment for the various departments that will be occupying the
facility.

Bond Issue (20000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.

*Referred to the Committee on Construction on 12/06/05.
Commissioner Hansen stated that what is lacking is an analysis of the comprehensive cost impact to the
tax payers and on the County Budget. This analysis must include an estimate of the needs of the County
Clerk and the Clerk of the Circuit Court.
Michael LaMont replied that before the warehouse was purchased, the main proposed tenants were in
attendance for the site visits with the Office of Capital Planning and Policy team. Since that time many
meetings have been conducted with all of the users. At this time it is still being detennined what exactly
the Clerk of the Circuit Court is going to need in the warehouse. $1.6 million has been budgeted for
telecom wiring in the warehouse; this was not included in the thought process because the County Clerk
had not yet determined what type of election equipment was going to be purchased.

Commissioner Hansen requested that the Committee on Construction receive a comprehensive
report from whomever President Stroger dictates. This comprehensive report should include what
will be going inside the warehouse, the estimated costs and the compatibility of the systems that will
be in the warehouse so that they will be interchangeable. T he report should be received by the
Committee on Construction within one month.
Al Riley, Planner, Office of Capital Planning and Policy, stated that the report dated September 5, 2003,
states that all of the figures are estimates.

333

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

Mr. LaMont stated that on December 13, 2005, he received a letter from the Clerk of the Circuit Court
stating that they were working with individuals to develop the retrieval systems; this letter also stated that
in January the Clerk of Circuit Court would have something to discuss with the Office of Capital Planning
and Policy. At this time, the County Clerk is having consultants examine warehousing systems for the
voting machines; they have come to the conclusion that the racking systems will not work. The industrial
engineers are the best individuals to conduct the study. He is not certain that the study will be completed
within one month.
Commissioner Hansen stated that the industrial engineers need to review material handling system
options and submit estimates to the Commissioners.
Commissioner Hansen stated that the industrial engineers need to develop a system and submit estimates
to the Commissioners.

Commissioner Collins, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved the approval of Communication
No. 274495. The motion carried.
274496

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated November 17, 2005:
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for the Purchasing Agent to advertise
for bids for the Countywide Pavement Restoration Program, Phase 2 at the Robbins, Ford
Heights, and Englewood Health Clinics, the Forensic Building, the 3rd District
Courthouse in Rolling Meadows, and the Rockwell and Hawthorne Warehouses. It is
respectfully requested that this Honorable Body approve this request.
Reason:

The second phase of this project provides for the repair or replacement of
asphalt parking lots and roadways. It also provides for concrete repair or
replacement of sidewalks, stairways, handicap ramps, curbs, and gutters.
This work will be part of an ongoing Countywide Pavement capital
improvement program.

Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.

*Referred to the Committee on Construction on 12/06/05.
Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Collins, moved the approval of Communication
No. 274496. The motion carried.
274497

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated November 17, 2005:

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Michael E. LaMont, Director,

external security features will be developed to further secure the building.
This renovation is required to convert the infrastructure of the building to
meet the needs of the County and to customize the layout of the facility to
satisfy the needs of the intended user groups.

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Family Court and Juvenile Detention Center Subcommittee of the Board of Commissioners of Cook
County met pursuant to notice on Thursday, December 15, 2005 at the hour of 10:00 A.M. in the Board
Room, Room 569, County Building, 118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Subcommittee has considered the following items and, upon adoption of this report, the
recommendations are as follows:
272882

RESOLUTION CALLING FOR A REVIEW OF THE COOK COUNTY JUVENILE
TEMPORARY DETENTION CENTER BY AN INDEPENDENT PANEL (PROPOSED
RESOLUTION). Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by Earlean Collins,
County Commissioner.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, Cook County is a home rule unit of local government pursuant to Article
VII Section 6(a) of the 1970 Illinois Constitution, and as such may exercise any power
and perform any function pertaining to its government and affairs; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County government has the responsibility for funding, operating
and monitoring the Cook County Juvenile Temporary Detention Center; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners is committed to insuring the
safety and welfare of minors in accordance with Federal, State and local ordinances on
juvenile detention; and
WHEREAS, over the past several years there has been increasing allegations in
reference to the treatment of children, the quality of staff, management and operating
procedures which has made it necessary for the Board to investigate the validity of such
charges.

341

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that an independent panel be appointed by
the President and approved by the Board of Commissioners to review the operation of the
Cook County Juvenile Temporary Detention Center which shall include, but not limited
to, the following areas:









Disciplinary actions taken toward youth;
The usage of both prescription and non-prescription drugs;
Sexual abuse;
Limitations placed on visitation;
The administrative structure;
The chain of command;
Staff development and training; and
Working conditions.

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the panel conduct its business and report
immediate findings of any inhumane treatment or danger to children and that all other
findings and recommendations shall be reported within five months.
*Referred to the Family Court and Juvenile Detention Center Subcommittee on
12/08/05.
*Deferred on 12/15/05.
Commissioner Steele, seconded by Commissioner Quigley,
Communication No. 272882. The motion carried.
274184

moved to

receive and file

RESOLUTION CALLING FOR IMMEDIATE VO LUNT ARY COMPLIANCE WITH
THE MEMORANDUM OF AGREEMENT FOR THE COOK COUNTY JUVENILE
TEMPORARY DETENTION CENTER (PROPOSED RESOLUTION). Submitting a
Proposed Resolution sponsored by Mike Quigley; Co-sponsored by Anthony J. Peraica,
County Commissioners.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

RESOLUTION CALLING FOR IMMEDIATE VOLUNTARY COMPLIANCE
WITH THE MEMORANDUM OF AGREEMENT FOR THE COOK COUNTY
JUVENILE TEMPORARY DETENTION CENTER
WHEREAS, in 1999, the American Civil Liberties Union (ACLU) and the MacArthur
Justice Center sued Cook County for civil rights violations, because of the conditions at
the Cook County Juvenile Temporary Detention Center (JTDC), citing that the children
at the center live in "an atmosphere of violence and fear"; and
WHEREAS, that lawsuit led to a Memorandum of Agreement (MOA) between Cook
County and the plaintiffs and the court's appointment of independent monitors to oversee
implementation of the MOA; and
WHEREAS, in October 2005, our two independent, court-appointed monitors issued
reports citing continuing dangerous conditions at the JTDC; and
WHEREAS, the court-appointed monitors reported persistent and ongoing problems at
the JTDC, including staff members' inappropriate use of force against the children,
vacant positions, and an overall inability of Cook County to fulfill the obligations of the
Memorandum of Agreement; and

342

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

WHEREAS, the exposure of our youth to this type of environment creates a generation
of future inmates at the Cook County Jail; and
WHEREAS, recognizing this, the ACLU has petitioned the court to declare Cook
County in violation of the decree and order Cook County's compliance w ith the decree in
six months.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that to avoid further delay in remedying
the deplorable conditions of the JTDC and to avoid protracted and expensive litigation,
the Cook County Board shall voluntarily comply with all terms of the Memorandum of
Agreement; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners calls
upon the President, in cooperation w ith the plaintiffs, our court-appointed monitors of the
JTDC, and subject to the approval of the Cook County Board of Commissioners, to
appoint a blue ribbon panel of recognized experts in juvenile corrections within 30 days
of the passage of this Resolution; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the panel shall, within 60 days of the passage of
this Resolution, conduct and complete a national search for a capable and independent
manager, with expertise in juvenile correctional planning and administration, to devise an
Implementation Plan to correct the deficiencies at the JTDC, per the Memorandum of
Agreement; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the President shall consider and accept the
recommendation of the blue-ribbon panel and shall appoint him or her to serve as the
independent manager, subject to the approval of the Cook County Board of
Commissioners; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that subsequent to the appointment of the independent
manager, the President and the Cook County Board of Commissioners shall take all
necessary steps to execute the manager's Implementation Plan and shall ensure that the
JTDC ultimately complies with the Memorandum of Agreement within six months of
passage of this Resolution.
*Referred to the Family Court and Juvenile Detention Center Subcommittee on
11115/05.
Patrick Driscoll, Deputy State's Attorney, Chief, Civil Actions Bureau, delivered the following
comments: There is a pending case in the United States District Court before Judge John A. Nordberg,
entitled Doe v. Cook County. The defendants in this case are Cook County and Jerry Robinson in his
official capacity as Superintendent of the Juvenile Temporary Detention Center. This case arises out of a
suit brought by the American Civil Liberties Union several years ago. There was a Memorandum of
Agreement relating to the Juvenile Temporary Detention Center entered into by both parties, the plaintiff
(a class action group) and Cook County. Presently, the Memorandum of Agreement is still in force and is
enforceable. Recently there have been additional filings by the plaintiff to compel enforcement of the
Memorandum of Agreement. The County has responded to that petition and has filed a response. The
Court has not issued a formal rule to show cause. The County is due next before the Court on January 11 ,
2006.

Commissioner Quigley moved approval of Communication No. 274184, seconded by Commissioner
Peraica. Commissioner Peraica called for a Roll Call, the vote of yeas and nays being as follows:

recommendations are as follows:
274510

CITY OF CHICAGO (NO CASH BID REQUEST). Transmitting a Communication
from Deborah Sims, Chairman, Tax Delinquency Subcommittee, submitting a request
from Lori T. Healy, Commissioner, City of Chicago.
The City of Chicago would like to request your support for its upcoming no-cash bid
under the Tax Reactivation Program (TRP). The issue will come before the Board in
next month's meeting. The TRP has proven itself to be an exceedingly beneficial
program for the City of Chicago. It has facilitated the acquisition and development of tax
delinquent parcels.
The objective of the Tax Reactivation Program is to produce affordable housing for low
and moderate income citizens. Also, the program develops blighted, vacant, dilapidated
and tax delinquent properties in commercial and industrial areas.
In the upcoming Scavenger Sale the City hopes to acquire parcels using the TRP. The
City has no " Third Party Requestor". The City of Chicago is excited by the prospect of
transforming tax delinquent properties into revenue properties benefiting their immediate
communities and the city as a whole.

2745 I I

CITY OF MARKHAM (NO CASH BID REQUEST). Transmitting a Communication
from Deborah Sims, Chainnan, Tax Delinquency Subcommittee, submitting a request
from David Webb, Jr., Mayor, City of Markham.
Re:

Cook County No Cash Bid Request from the City of Markham

The City of Markham is hereby submitting a no cash bid application of 70 parcels for
scavenger sale or over-the-counter bids. Redevelopment will benefit the City with new
tax revenue, new residents and new economic activity.
Project Description: This project is in the very beginning stage and the no cash bid
request is the first step. The parcels are in an area that was unincorporated Cook County
until recently. The City annexed the parcels in the past year. The parcels are vacant land
and lack full infrastructure. The City seeks to build new single family homes. Site plans
have not been drawn as the City is researching density issues and plating to best facilitate
new residential use. Infrastructure upgrades and layout are also being researched in order
to best determine the development scope and layout. The acquisition of land from
adjacent owners is also being researched. Columbia Properties, Inc. is the third party
requester. Columbia Properties has an excellent track record with Markham and has the
confidence of the City Council and the City Administration. Completed projects by
Columbia include one single family home and a new commercial building for a
Walgreen's. Columbia is also going forward on new construction of a residential town
home project that has been approved by the City.
The City will retain legal counsel, obtain tax deeds and pay all acquisition costs. The City
will report as required to the Cook County Office of Economic Development annually
from the date of sale on each parcel for five years or until the development is completed,
whichever occurs last.

RESOLUTIONS
06-R-29
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE LARRY SUFFREDIN, JOHN P. DALEY AND EARLEAN COLLINS
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
FORREST CLAYPOOL, ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN,
CARL R. HANSEN, ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO,
JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA, MIKE QUIGLEY,
PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS AND BOBBIE L. STEELE
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
RECOGNIZING THE CENTER FOR ECONOMIC PROGRESS
WHEREAS, the Center for Economic Progress was established in 1990 as a non-profit organization; and
WHEREAS, the mission of the Center for Economic Progress is to increase economic opportunity for
low-income families, children and individuals by improving access to public, private and non-profit
programs and services; through direct services, public education and advocacy, the Center challenges
barriers facing its constituency, thus encouraging self-sufficiency and promoting economic prosperity;
and
WHEREAS, in 2005, through its Tax Counseling Project, more than 900 Center volunteers encouraged
the use of the earned income tax credit and prepared over 25,000 tax returns bringing back more than $35
million in refunds to hard-working Illinois families; and
WHEREAS, the Tax Counseling Project was launched at four Chicago homeless shelters in 1994 and has
grown in only ten years to become the nation's largest free statewide tax preparation service for working
fami lies and individuals; and
WHEREAS, trained volunteers participating in the Tax Counseling Project provide free tax preparation
assistance for families with incomes of $36,000 or less and individuals with incomes of $ 15,000 or less at
sites located across Illinois, approximately 1,200 of which are in Cook County; and
WHEREAS, between January 28 and April 15, 2006, the Tax Counseling Project will offer services in 35
communities in the greater Cook County Area including Auburn Gresham, Back of the Yards, Humboldt
Park, Rogers Park, West Garfield Park, Woodlawn and Harvey; and
WHEREAS, the Center for Economic Progress is a member of the National Community Tax Coalition
which has over 300 affiliates from 40 states; the Coalition works to dramatically increase access to tax
credits, benefits and asset-building opportunities for low-and moderate-low income individuals, fami lies
and communities; and

358

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005
WHEREAS, the Center for Economic Progress is widely recognized as an important community
resource.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby thank the Center for Economic Progress for its service to the people of Cook County; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County requests that all
Cook County elected officials and all County officials make information about the Tax Counseling
Project available in their offices where the general public would be present; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the Center for
Economic Progress as a symbol of this auspicious occasion.

Approved and adopted this 21st day of December 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved
and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

Transmitting a Communication, dated December 7, 2005 from
MARK KILGALLON, Chief, Bureau of Human Resources
Transmitting herewith is a renewal of a Resolution concerning military benefits for your consideration
and approval at the December 21, 2005 Board Meeting.
06-R-30
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS,
JOHN P. DALEY, ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN,
CARL R. HANSEN, ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO,
JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA, MIKE QUIGLEY,
PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, the United States has continued to undertake military reserve operations in response to the
terrorist acts against the United States of America, known as Operations Noble Eagle, Enduring/Iraqi
Freedom, as well as national interest endeavors worldwide; and

359

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 2 1, 2005

WHEREAS, employees of the County of Cook who are members of the military reserve force of the
United States or of the State of Illinois have been called to active duty, which has caused an economic
hardship upon such employees and their families; and
WHEREAS, it is the intent of the Cook County Board to provide transitional assistance to such
employees and their families while they are adjusting to the changed set of circumstances.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners:
I.

In addition to the paid eleven-day leave of absence provided in Section 9-1 5 of the
Ordinances and Resolutions of Cook County, Illinois, governing military leave and
applicable collective bargaining agreements, employees of Cook County who are
members of the reserve force of the State of lllinois who have been or are ordered to
active duty by appropriate authorities shall be eligible for additional paid leave and
benefits, as provided for herein.

2.

The Chainnan of the Committee on Finance, the Chief of the Bureau of Human
Resources, and the President' s des ignated Chief Financial Officer, or thei r designees,
shall constitute the Military Benefits Committee. The Committee shall promulgate
eligibility standards for additional paid leave and length thereof based on criteria,
including, but not limited to, length of service and job performance, and shall develop
procedures for application for such benefits by employees. Paid leave shall be in
amounts equal to the employees regular monthly salary minus his/her military base pay
compensation. Benefits to be continued for employees called to military duty under this
Ordinance shall include continuation of family medical coverage under the plan currently
in force for each employee. The Committee will approve or disapprove such applications
based on the application for additional paid leave and the applicant's employment
information contained in Cook County records. The Committee shall report to the Cook
County Board of Commissioners each denial of an application for additional paid leave
within thirty days after the denial.

3.

Additional paid leave hereunder shall automatically terminate upon the termination of
active duty in connection with active duty status.

4.

No additional paid leave hereunder shall be payable after December 3 1, 2006.

Approved and adopted this 21st day of December 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Murphy, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

Transmitting a Communication, dated December 1, 2005 from
PETER C. NICHOLSON, Director, Department of Planning and Development
Re:

J.P. Diemond, LLC
Resolution Approving Class 6b Special Exception to Abandonment

respectfully submitting this Resolution regarding the J.P. Diemond, LLC application for Class 6b
property tax incentive for your consideration.

361

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

J.P. Diemond, LLC requests approval of the special exception to the 24 month abandonment rule under
the Class 6b Ordinance. This Resolution is required so that the company can complete its application to
the Assessor of Cook County.
J.P. Diemond, LLC's application for a Class 6b, the Resol ution of the City of Chicago, Illinois, and a
Department of Planning and Development staff report have been submitted for your information.
06-R-32
RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has adopted a Real Property Assessment
Classification 6b that provides an applicant a reduction in the assessment level for an industrial facility;
and
WHEREAS, the County Board of Commissioners has received and reviewed an application from J.P.
Diemond, LLC and the Resolution from the City of Chicago for an abandoned industrial facility located
at 4237 West 42nd Place, Chicago, Cook County, Illinois, Property Index Number 19-03-200-031-0000;
and
WHEREAS, Class 6b requires the validation by the County Board of the shortened period of qualifying
abandonment in cases where the industrial facility has been abandoned for less than 24 consecutive
months upon purchase; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the building was abandoned
for 11.5 months at the time of application and that special circumstances are present.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and Board of Commissioners of the
County of Cook, State of Illinois, that the President and Board of Commissioners indicate their approval
for the filing of an application for a Cook County Real Estate Classification 6b abatement incentive to J.P.
Diemond, LLC for an abandoned industrial facility located at 4237 West 42nd Place, Chicago, Cook
County, Illinois, under the provision for abandonment of less than 24 months; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk is hereby authorized and directed to forward a
certified copy of this Resolution to the Office of the Cook County Assessor.
Approved and adopted this 21st day of December 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Collins, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

the County Clerk, page 442.

Evergreen Palmer, LLC
Resolution Approving Class 6b Special Exception to Abandonment

respectfully submitting this Resolution regarding the Evergreen Palmer, LLC application for Class 6b
property tax incentive for your consideration.
Evergreen Palmer, LLC requests approval of the special exception to the 24 month abandonment rule
under the Class 6b Ordinance. This Resolution is required so that the company can complete its
application to the Assessor of Cook County.
Evergreen Palmer, LLC's application for a Class 6b, the Resolution of the Village of Schaumburg,
Illinois, and a Department of Planning and Development staff report have been submitted for your
information.
06-R-33
RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has adopted a Real Property Assessment
Classification 6b that provides an applicant a reduction in the assessment level for an industrial facility;
and
WHEREAS, the County Board of Commissioners has received and reviewed an application from
Evergreen Palmer, LLC and the Resolution from the Village of Schaumburg for an abandoned industrial
facility located at 2401 Palmer Drive, Schaumburg, Cook County, Illinois, Property Index Numbers 0234-300-060-0000 and 02-34-300-061-0000; and
WHEREAS, Class 6b requires the validation by the County Board of the shortened period of qualifying
abandonment in cases where the industrial facility has been abandoned for less than 24 consecutive
months upon purchase; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the building was abandoned
for 17 months at the time of application and that special circumstances are present.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and Board of Commissioners of the
County of Cook, State of Illinois, that the President and Board of Commissioners indicate their approval
for the filing of an application for a Cook County Real Estate Classification 6b abatement incentive to
Evergreen Palmer, LLC for an abandoned industrial facility located at 240 I Palmer Drive, Schaumburg,
Cook County, Illinois, under the provision for abandonment of less than 24 months; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk is hereby authorized and directed to forward a
certified copy of this Resolution to the Office of the Cook County Assessor.

IN MEMORY OF LESTER BROWNSTEIN
WHEREAS, Niles Township Trustee Lester Brownstein was born in Chicago and passed away at the age
of 84 on December 5, 2005; and
WHEREAS, a lifelong resident of Cook County, Lester Brownstein graduated from Senn High School
and honorably served in the Am1y in the South Pacific during World War II ; and
WHEREAS, Lester Brownstein was the beloved husband of Hollis Rizer, proud father of Barbara,
Steven Louis, Steven David and Dennis Jay and doting grandfather to his seven grandchildren; and
WHEREAS, Lester Brownstein was elected Niles Township Trustee in 1999 and was a Trustee at the
time of his death; and
WHEREAS, prior to beginning his career in government, Mr. Brownstein was a vice president for sales
at Atlas Steel Corp. in Chicago and in the late 1950s, started Fox Steel, a steel distributor in Chicago; and
WHEREAS, upon closing Fox Steel, Lester Brownstein joined the Illinois Secretary of State's Office as
the manager of the Melrose Park drivers services facility and then worked as the assistant manager of the
Niles facility where he remained until his retirement in the late 1990s; and
WHEREAS, in addition to working in public service for the State of Illinois, Lester Brownstein was
deeply committed to the democratic process and was very active in local politics; and

365

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005

driving force behind the Morton Grove Caucus Party; above all, Mr. Brownstein worked to correct
injustices and find creative solutions to local problems; and
WHEREAS, Lester Brownstein was a fonner code enforcement officer for Morton Grove and in 1993,
was appointed to the position of Niles Township Collector, a post he held until he was elected Township
Trustee in 1999; and
WHEREAS, Lester Brownstein served his community for most of his life and continued working in
public service even as most of his peers were enjoying their retirement; Mr. Brownstein was serving as
the Director of Township Officials of the Cook County Trustees Division at the time of his passing; and
WHEREAS, Lester Brownstein is fondly remembered by his family and friends as a man who loved life,
delighted in meeting new people, appreciated a good party and always tried to have fun; and
WHEREAS, Lester Brownstein used his talents to improve the quality of life for the residents of Morton
Grove and Niles Township.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the famil y and friends of Lester
Brownstein and joins them in sorrow at this time of loss; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the family of Lester
Brownstein so that his memory may be so honored and ever cherished.

IN MEMORY OF HAROLD D. SHAPIRO
WHEREAS, Harold D. Shapiro was born on April 15, 1927 in Chicago and died on December l , 2005 at
the age of78; and
WHEREAS, Harold Shapiro was a decorated World War II veteran who enlisted in the Navy in 1944 and
served with the Seabees, the Naval Construction Battalion, on Samar in the Philippine Islands; and
following his tour of duty, Harold served four years as a reservist until his honorable discharge in 1950;
and
WHEREAS, Harold Shapiro earned undergraduate and law degrees from Northwestern University and as
a Jaw student, was editor-in-chief of the university's law review; and
WHEREAS, Harold Shapiro, a Wilmette resident, practiced law at Sonnenschein, Nath & Rosenthal,
LLP for nearly 53 years, 4 7 of them as partner, and served as the firm 's first chairman from 1985 to 1990;
and
WHEREAS, Mr. Shapiro's legal accomplishments are numerous and include representing Allstate
Insurance for more than 50 years, directing the legal work when Allstate went public, serving as outside
counsel for the sale of the Sears Tower and developing Sonnenschein offices coast-to-coast; and
WHEREAS, in addition to practicing law, Harold Shapiro was passionate about legal education; he
lectured and taught at Northwestern University School of Law for 46 years and in 1971 was named the
Senior Edward A. Harriman Adjunct Professor of Law; and
WHEREAS, in his free time, Harold Shapiro was a golf enthusiast, regularly played basketball, enjoyed
reading, was passionate about politics and was a lifelong devoted White Sox fan; and
WHEREAS, Harold Shapiro was the beloved husband of Beatrice, proud father of Matthew, Michal Ann
and Nicholas and doting grandfather of Daniel, Martin and Sarah; and
WHEREAS, Harold Shapiro is fondly remembered by his family, friends and colleagues as a man who
loved life, a natural teacher and mentor and as someone who was always willing to help those in need;
and
WHEREAS, With his countless contributions and leadership roles to organizations such as Junior
Achievement of Chicago, Schwab Hospital Foundation and Rehabilitation Hospital and the Northwestern
Memorial Foundation's Professional Council for Philanthropy and his work to promote affordable
housing in Chicago, Harold Shapiro used his talents on a daily basis to improve the quality of life for the
residents of Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the loss of Harold Shapiro has a deep impact on the legal, civic and philanthropic
communities in Chicago and the nation that will be felt for many years to come.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family, friends and colleagues of
Harold D . Shapiro and joins them in sorrow at this time ofloss; and

367

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the family of Harold
D. Shapiro and Sonnenschein, Nath & Rosenthal, LLP so that his memory may be so honored and ever
cherished.

Approved and adopted this 21st day of December 2005.

WHEREAS, Cezar "Cid" Milorad Froelich was born on January I, 1946 in Walcz, Poland or
Deutschkrone, Germany depending on who controlled the area; and
WHEREAS, Cid Froehlich's family immigrated to the United States and he became a naturalized citizen
in 1958; and
WHEREAS, Cid Froehlich married his beloved wife Mary Anita Bannes on August 24, 1968; Cid and
Mary are the proud parents of Jennifer, Christian and Michael; and
WHEREAS, in addition to being a loving dedicated father, Cid delights in being a doting grandfather to
twins James and Olivia; and
WHEREAS, Cid received his bachelor's degree from Loyola University of Chicago and graduated from
the Loyola University of Chicago School of Law in 1970; and
WHEREAS, one of Cid's early jobs as a lawyer was working as a Staff Attorney with the United States
Securities and Exchange Commission; and
WHEREAS, Cid is a founding partner of Shefsky and Froelich, Ltd. concentrating in corporate, gaming,
mergers and acquisitions and securities law; and
WHEREAS, Shefsky and Froelich has grown under Cid's leadership from a three lawyer firm in 1975 to
an 80 lawyer firm today; and
WHEREAS, an accomplished lawyer, Cid has authored numerous articles, spoken at a variety of
conferences on securities and gaming law and is a lecturer at the DePaul University College of Law; and
WHEREAS, Cid is an accomplished golfer and fisherman who shares his great love of sport with all; and
WHEREAS, Cid is respected and admired by the many friends and colleagues whose lives he has
touched.

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to Cezar "Cid" Milorad
Froelich as a symbol of this auspicious occasion.
