06-R-44
RESOL UTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE CARL R. HANSEN, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JOHN P. DALEY,
JERRY BUTLER, FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS,
ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN, ROBERTO MALDONADO,
JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA,
MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, Sonya Crawshaw was called from our midst on December 19, 2005 at the age of 67; and
WHEREAS, Sonya Crawshaw served the Village of Hanover Park as President from 1985 to 1997; and
WHEREAS, Sonya Crawshaw also served the Village of Hanover Park as Clerk for 12 years before her
three terms as President; and

376

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005
WHEREAS, as one of the first female municipal chief executives in the area, Sonya Crawshaw helped
the Turnberry Lakes Business Park to prosper and inspired the creation of a fire department run and
funded by Hanover Park; and
WHEREAS, Sonya Crawshaw served as President of the Northwest Municipal Conference; and
WHEREAS, Sonya Crawshaw served as President of the Du Page Mayors and Managers Conference;
and
WHEREAS, Sonya Crawshaw earned the Volunteer Service Award from the U.S. President's Council on
Service and Civic Participation for her generous volunteer activity on behalf of several organizations; and
WHEREAS, Sonya Crawshaw gave her time to the American Cancer Society, the Read to Learn adult
literacy program with Schaumburg Township, the Boy Scouts of Northwest Suburban Cook County, and
to the Madrigal Singers of Hoffman Estates High School; and
WHEREAS, Sonya Crawshaw contributed greatly to the community of Hanover Park as a public official
and as a volunteer; now, therefore,
BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does hereby express its profound
sorrow at the death of Sonya Crawshaw and extends its heartfelt condolences to her entire family.

Approved and adopted this 21st day of December 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

06-R-45
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY,
ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN,
ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, ANTHONY J. PERAICA,
MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, Robert Gooley was the loving husband of sixty-four years of Marion; devoted father of
Barbara; beloved grandfather of two grandchildren and two great grandchildren; and

377

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21, 2005

WHEREAS, Robert Gooley was born in New Haven, Connecticut, in 19 17 and grew up on Chicago' s
Southeast Side. He married his high school sweetheart, took over the Russell Steel Company which he
eventually owned and moved to Homewood in the early 1950s. Mr. Gooley became a strong leader of his
community, deeply dedicated and committed to improving the quality of life of the residents there; and
WHEREAS, Robert Gooley valiantly served his country as a sergeant in the Army during World War II,
fighting in the Pacific Theater at Guadalcanal; and
WHEREAS, Robert Gooley's three decade political career was sparked by his passionate, successful
campaign for a baseball diamond for the children of his Homewood neighborhood; and
WHEREAS, Robert Gooley worked tirelessly as Homewood Zoning Commissioner in the 1960s and
1970s and also served as a Homewood Village trustee in the 1970s; and
WHEREAS, Robert Gooley served as Homewood Village President from 1978 to 1985. The widening
of l 83rd Street and bringing Lake Michigan water to the suburb are two of his most ambitious
accomplishments; and
WHEREAS, Robert Gooley served as a Cook County Commissioner from 1986 to 1994 where he
successfully fought for the right of municipalities to have input on zoning issues in adjacent
unincorporated areas; and
WHEREAS, Robert Gooley was an avid golfer and a member of the Olympia Fields Country Club. He
supervised the maintenance of Cook County public courses after his retirement as Commissioner; and
WHEREAS, Robert Gooley was genuinely admired and respected by his many friends and colleagues
and was honored when the board room of the Homewood Village Hall was named for him in 1998.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family and friends of Robert
Gooley and joins them in sorrow at this time ofloss; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the family of Robert
Gooley as recognition of his good works and that his memory may be so honored and ever cherished.

Approved and adopted this 21 st day of December 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAYID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.

adopted. President Stroger called for a rising vote. The motion carried unanimously.

COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, for the last ten years Mr. Michael LaMont has served Cook County as the Director of the
Office of Capital Planning and Policy with exemplary performance and sincere dedication; and
WHEREAS, in 2003 Michael LaMont received the Government Civil Engineer of the Year Award; and
WHEREAS, this award was based on his established reputation for professional service and his notable
success in improving the conditions under which professional engineers serve in the public sector; and
WHEREAS, Mr. LaMont distinguished himself in the guidance and development of young civil
engineers, and through other continuing achievements in his field; and
WHEREAS, Mr. LaMont's integrity, hard work and keen sense of detail have provided his staff and
colleagues with an important leadership example; and
WHEREAS, under his guidance, Capital Planning' s public projects have been managed with the highest
level of professionalism and subsequently with a consistent level of achievement; and
WHEREAS, Mr. LaMont's legacy is forever etched in the history of Cook County for his management in
overseeing the planning, design and construction of the John H. Stroger, Jr. Hospital of Cook County; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Lamont successfully ensured that this enormous $600 million public works
construction project was completed on-time and within budget; and
WHEREAS, he simultaneously directed the design and construction of numerous other public facilities,
including six new healthcare clinics, a new hospital for jail inmates and a new domestic violence
courthouse; and
WHEREAS, Mr. LaMont also successfully implemented the practice of Countywide innovations for
various projects, including roofs, elevators and fire alarm systems.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and Members of the Board of
Commissioners on behalf of the more than the five million residents of Cook County, does hereby extend
our sincere gratitude for all of your hard work and dedication during your ten years as Director of the
Office of Capital Planning and Policy; and

379

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 21 , 2005

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that a copy of same be tendered to Michael LaMont in honor of
his dedication to County government.
Approved and adopted this 21st day of December 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
